The method of fumigation is that you take a pot with charcoal embers and cover it with a pewter lid pierced in the middle, and insert the shoulder into the instrument; then apply the fumigation, and instruct the patient to place the cheekbone against his mouth, sealing it so the smoke does not escape but travels upwards; and the afflicted area will now improve, and if it doesn't come out, repeat the fumigation many times; and let the patient endure thirst, eating rotten things and ash, without drinking any water; and eventually, this management must be followed.

li chapistres des apostemes	If the shape should have abrasions; ensure smoothness or the surface where you can easily insert. Mout de semblances d’aposteme sont, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient ci aprés d’un et d’autre en cest livre, et sont diver en perforation et en taille; et c’est en II manieres dont l’une est en sa semblance meisme, et de ceu qu’il tient moistor.	 There are many types of abscesses, as recounted here in this book from one to another, and they differ by perforation and incision; there are two ways it occurs, one being the same and due to moisture.

car li apostemes dou chief est autres que cil dou fondement, et li apostemes dou leu charnut est autres que cil qui vient en jointures, et chescuns ait son jugement en l’uevre.	 because the abscesses on the head are different from those at the base, and the abscesses within muscles are different from those that arise in joints, each has its own judgment in practice.
Et si a apostemes c’on ne doit mie percier, tant que li bowe est meure selonc son acomplissement; et si a de telz qu’il covient percier quant il sont crut, et ne meurent mie selonc lor acomplissement, si com aposteme qui sont delez jointures.	 And if with abscesses one must not cut until the swelling is dead according to its completion; and with those that it requires cutting when they are ripe, and do not die according to their completion, like an abscess near a joint.
Car quant apostemes vient delez jointures, et on le laisse tant qu’il est porris entor, par aventure si sont corrumput li liien et li nerf de la jointure, par coi ce est cause de contraction en celui membre.	 When abscesses occur near the joints and are left until they ripen, through chance these may rot the ligament and nerve of the joint, causing contraction in that limb.
Ou li aposteme est delez lou membre principel, et se tu tardes la perforation tant qu’il soit meurez, si nuira au membre principeil; ou il est delez lou fondement, si le perce on ainsois qu’il soit meurs; et ne covient mie que tu perces aposteme crut sens digestion acomplie, fuers que celui qui est delez lou fondement, qu’il ne porrisse em parfont, et soit alongiez dedens, et i viegne fistule; et ne puisse saner en grant termine.	 When the abscess is near the main limb and if you delay puncturing until it dies, it will harm the main limb; or if it is near the base, pierce as soon as it ripens; do not perforate an abscess that has just completed digestion, except for those near the base, preventing them from bursting, and being spread within, leading to a fistula; so they cannot heal completely.
Et covient que tu saiches l’oure de la perforation de l’aposteme qui est meur selonc l’acomplissement, et c’est quant li dolor est apaisie, et li departemens de la fievre, et l’amenuisement de la dolor et de la roujor, et dou debatement et de l’aguisement dou chief de l’aposteme, et les autres signes; et covient que tu faices seoir la perforation ou plus dependant leu de l’aposteme, et la ou il apert mues; et soit li perforation dou lonc dou cors, et se li apostemes est as mains ou as piez, ou en jointures et au ners et as arteres, et en toz leus igalz ou il n’a point de ploieure.	And if ite ait quant perciex la tire, si on les maniere est semblant doumes oltieremme. ûs'en que tu ne li aspertenent: et li croistement li apoteme en l’aposteme du mesl; and cest lorz est as pienli ou il a lea tiz qui seiz li chiete, si le metre quant a la percer.
En ces que ploient, par selonc celui membre.	 In cases where it bulges, according to that limb.
Et quant apostemes est en leu charnut, si vaut mues que tu laisses la perforation tant qu’il soit confermez en digestion acomplie, si com nos avons dit.	 When abscesses are ready to burst, it is necessary to leave the puncture until digestion is completed as we have said.
Car se tu lou perces devant ceu, si iert alongiez li cors dou venim de lui, et est plains de mout d’ordure; et par aventure endurcissent les levres et li parfondetez de lui.	 For if you pierce it in front of this (point), the body's poison spreads throughout it, and it is filled with much filth; and sometimes the lips harden and its deepest parts.

Li ancien dirent et parlerent de la tailleure de la gorge; mais je ne vis onques en nostre terre qui la feist, et c’est li escripture de lor parole.	The ancients spoke and wrote of throat surgery; however, I have never seen it done in our land, and this is according to their writings.

Poc avient que piere soit enjanree en femmes, et s’il avient aucune fois, si est li cure grief, et est deffendut por .iij. choses: l’une est que per aventure li femme est vierge; et li seconde est c’on ne puet trover femme bien saichant qui se descuevre as mires, meismement quant elle est caste.	It often happens that stones are found in women, and if it occurs repeatedly, the condition is serious, and there are three reasons to avoid it: one is that perhaps the woman is a virgin; and the second is that one cannot find a well-informed woman who will uncover herself before the mirrors, especially when she is chaste.

Et li ancien dirent qu’ele est faite si com li ramice qui est ensamble la vis, en teil maniere que tu lie les vasselz, aprés la taille sus ous legierement au desoz; puis cope em mi, et cure l’aposteme de ceu qui oevre, tant que li vasselz chient; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And the ancients said that it is made like a joint being put together with a screw, in such a way that you fasten the vessels after shaping them slightly over the bone; then wrap and cover, and treat the abscess from what works, until the threads fall off; and cure it as we have said, until it heals perfectly.
Aucune fois vient routure ens angres, si com nos avons dit, et apert li leus; et ne dessent nulz des intestines as coions, et s’il en i dessent, c’est poc, et repaire toutes houres; et toutevoie s’il demoure trop en cest point, si croit li plaie ou syphac, tant que li intestine dessent; et ceu avient par l’estension dou syfac qui est as angres, si com nos avons dit, car il est estendus, puis est mollifiez et enflez li leus et apert; et li cure si est par cautere, si com nos avons devant dit; et aucune fois est curee par fer en ceste maniere: et est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos entre tes mains, puis cope le leu de la routure enfleit dou large selonc la quantiteit de III dois; et puis estrai le syfac qui est desoz le cuir que l’ensuet, puis pren lou rait et lou met sor le leu apparant dou syfac; et lou presse au parfont dou ventre, puis cout les II leus apparans dou syfac sus lou chief dou rait, et cout l’un et l’autre; puis estrai le chief dou rait, et ne coper point dou syfac ne n’estendre l’uef n’autre chose, si com je t’ai fait savoir en la cure de la ramice des intestines; puis le cure par la cure des plaies.	 Never comes out the spleen, as we have said, and open the eyes; and no intestines come loose from their ligaments, and if they do, it's little, and all heal in hours; however, if it remains too long at this point, then a hernia or hydrocele occurs until the intestines slip out; and this happens through the extension of hydrocele within the antrum, as we have said, because it is stretched, then softened and swol cushioning and open. The treatment is done by caustic as we have previously mentioned: and that the patient lies on his back between your hands, then cover the enlarged area with a length according to the quantity of three fingers; and then extract the hydrocele under the skin layer from where it protrudes, then take the thread and place it over the visible part of the hydrocele on the head of the thread, and hold both. Then extract the top part of the thread, and do not cover or extend anything related to the scrotum, as I have previously explained in the treatment of intestinal coccyx with a suture; then treat it by wound care method.
Et quant tu copes les filz, si le mundefie et cure la plaie, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	 And when you bind the wounds, if they are unclean and treat the injury, until it is healed.
Li syfac est constrains, et n’a point d’apparance en la routure, et li cauteres est muedres en cest leu, et plus prochiens a salut.	The fistula is tight and has no external opening in the course, and the fire cautery is less effective at this location, and closer to being curable.
de l’amollissement dou cuir des coions	From the softening of the skin around the joints
Maintes fois est amollis li cuirs des coions en aucuns homes, por ceu que les chars que sont dedens sont mollifiees, et est lait a veoir; et est mestier, quant on le vuet curer, c’on faice gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li cope le cuir qui est mollifiez sus le cuir natureil; puis assemble les .ij. levres a une costure, et se tu vues, cout premier la superfluiteit dou cuir mollifiiez a .iij. costures ou .iiij. fermement; puis cope entre les costures, et lou cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez, et chient li fil.	Many times the skin around the joints is softened in some people because of moisture inside that becomes mollified and appears milky; when one wants to clean it, make the patient lie on their back with the affected area exposed, and clip off the overly mollified skin from the natural skin; then stitch together the two edges into a single seam, and if you look, do so first by removing the excess softened skin in three or four neatly placed sutures; then cut between the sutures, and treat the wound as with other wounds until it is healthy again.
dou chastrement	From the act of pounding
Saiches que chastremens est escomeniez en nostre loi, et por ceu il me plairoit que je n’en parlasse mie en cest livre; et n’est necessaires fuer que por II manieres: dont l’une est que li mires en saiche respondre quant on li demandera, et en saiche la cure; et li autre, por ceu que nos avons sovent mestier de chastrement d’aucunes bestes por nos aidier, si com de bouc et de mouton et de chait et d’autres bestes.	 I have heard of these afflictions in our laws, and for this reason, I would not speak of them in this book; however, there are two reasons why they are necessary: the first is that healers should respond when asked about them and their treatment, and the second, because we often need animal punishment to help us, such as with goats, sheep, donkeys, and other animals.
Je dis donques que chastremens est fais selonc II manieres: ou par atraction, ou par fendure.	 I say therefore that afflictions are caused in two ways: by attraction or by puncturing.
En celle que nos faisons par attraction, faisons nos seoir la beste en aigue chaude, tant que li coion soient mollifiez et pendant; puis les preing a ta main, tant qu’il soient remis et que tu ne les sentes plus.	 In the way we cause afflictions by attraction, we make the animal sit in hot water until its joints become soft and flexible; then pinch it with your hand until they are restored and no longer feel painful.
Du chastrement de taille: covient que tu teignes la beste, et li presse le cuir des coions a ta main senestre, puis lie le suspensoire, et cope sus chescun oef a I cop, quant tu les avras bien escorchiez; et i laisse aucun poc dou syfac et lou subtil syfac qui est sor les vasselz; et ceste maniere de chastrement est muedre que cele qui est faite par attraction, por ceu que a l’atraction demoure par aventure aucune chose des coions, par coi li beste desire luxure; puis cure la plaie tant qu’ele soit sanee.	 For the procedure of cutting: it is proper to hold the animal, and press its hide at the hocks with your left hand, then attach the suspender, and bind over each joint after you have properly scorched them; and leave no small part tender or subtil tendon near the bones; this method of cutting is more effective than that made by attraction because in the latter case some parts of the hocks may remain, causing the animal to desire lust. Then heal the wound until it is cured.
des hermofrodites	Hermaphrodites are individuals or organisms that possess both male and female reproductive organs, allowing them to produce either spermatozoa or eggs, depending on their species' biology. This condition can occur naturally in some plants, animals, and even humans (though human cases often result from specific genetic or hormonal factors). Hermaphroditism plays a significant role in the reproductive strategies of many organisms, allowing for diverse methods of reproduction such as self-fertilization or increased mating flexibility within populations.
Hermofrodie est selonc II manieres as homes: l’une si est que entre les II coions apert ausi com li figure de la nature d’une femme, ou il ait poil, et aucunes fois en cort li urine.	 A hermaphrodite is according to two ways in humans: one where between the two gonads they resemble as those of a woman's body, and sometimes it urinates there.
Et li autre maniere si est en femmes, et ait sus lou poignil ausi com une verge et II coions.	 And the other manner is among women, with swelling of their fingers like a rod and strings.
Et li cure de l’ome et de la fame si est que tu copes les chars ajostees toutes, et les cure si com autres plaies; en la seconde maniere, des homes dont li urine saut par lou cuir des coions, si n’a point de cure.	 And the treatment of men and women involves removing all stones from their bodies and curing them as with other wounds; in the second manner, for men whose urine shoots through the sheaths of strings, there is no remedy.
de la tentigene	Of the tempting nature
Tentigene est une chars ajostee sus la partie natureil, tant qu’elle est trop laide a veoir; et aucunes femmes l’ont ausi grant com une main, et c’est li cure.	 An inflamed stone is lodged in the natural part, too unsightly to look at; and some women have it as large as a hand, which requires treatment.
Il covient que tu teignes la superfluiteit de la tentigene a ta main ou as oncines, et la cope legierement; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et a une autre char que naist a la bouche de la marris, et l’emple, et par aventure saut fuer, et est selonc la semblance d’une kowe, et por ceu l’apelerent li ancien «maladie kowee».	 You must grasp the excess of the inflamed stone with your hand or fingers and remove it gently; and do not pull too hard to avoid bleeding, then treat it further until it is healthy again; and for another type that appears at the mouth of the urethra, which is inserted and sometimes forcefully expelled, and it resembles a cow, hence they called it in ancient times "malady cowee.
Si covient que tu la copes, si com nos avons dit la tentigene, et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	 If it is necessary to treat it as we have said in the experiment, and care for it until it is healed.
de erratique	Erratic refers to something that behaves in a way that is not predictable or consistent; in this context, likely referring to the erratic behavior of an inflammation.
Erratique si est quant li nature de la femme n’est mie percie, ou li pertus est petis; et est naturez par naissance, ou accidens par maladie que venue i est; ou c’est par char ajostee, ou dou syfac subtil ou espés, et est fais em parfont en la marris, ou en costez, ou desoz, ou que soit; et deffent le concevoir, et l’enfantement, et par aventure les flors a avoir; et li connoissance de ceu si est par le regart de la baile. Se li estoupemens est prochiens apparans, si quier a tes dois ou au rait.	 If the hernia appears nearing, either on your thighs or groin.

Emorroydes sont overtures de voines dont sans cort acostumeement, et quant les emorroydes sont vielles si devienent thelul; et nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’aus, et les signes, et je dirai ci celles qui resoivent curation. des apostemes de la marris	Abscesses of the anus
Maintes manieres d’aposteme vienent en la marris, si com chancre et aposteme pierous et herpes et estiomenes et fistules et emorroides et aposteme chaut, et plusors autres maladies que j’ai dit en la division. de l’enfantement	Of childbirth
Mestier est premier a la baile qu’elle conoisse la figure de l’enfantement natureil, et li signes si est quant tu vois la femme apresser aval, et desire odorer l’ar: adonques se haste li enfes de fuer issir; adonc saiches que cil enfantemens est selonc la figure natureil, et est li issue soz son chief, et li secondine avec lui; et quant tu vois ces signes, si covient presser legierement son ventre, si que li enfes isse tost; car quant il dessent sus son chief, si ist li secondine avec lui, et est mondee li marris de ses superfluitez par bone mundification; et cist qui vient autrement ne vient mie naturelment.	 It is necessary first for the midwife to know the natural shape of childbirth, and recognize the signs when a woman begins to dilate and desires to smell urine: then quickly comes the baby out; thus you know that such childbirths follow the natural figure, and the issue is from its head, with twins alongside it. And when you see these signs, one must gently press her belly so that the baby emerges soon because as it moves onto its head, there are accompanying twins, and the excessive membranes of its coverings have been properly cleansed; those who come otherwise do not naturally occur.
Car il vient aucune fois sus ses piez, et vient fuer li cors ou li chiés, et les mains, ou il vient sus son ventre, ou sovin, et est convertis par aventure sor son col, et par autres figures malvaises; si est mestier a la baile qu’elle soit saige et subtilz en ces choses, et se warse d’error et de decevement, et je vos mostrerai toutes les figures coment on li doit aidier.	 At times it comes upon his feet, and strikes the body or the head, and the hands, where it comes upon his belly, or behind him, and is turned by chance about his neck, and in other malicious ways; thus it is necessary for the healer to be wise and subtle in these matters, and to guard against error and deception, and I will show you all the figures as how one should assist.
Se li enfes vient sus son chief par issue natureil, et li femme enfante griement, et li vertus de li est foible, si la fai seoir sus une selle, ou les femmes la tienent; et arose sa nature d’oile ou fenugreic soit cuit, et puis boute li baile entre ses dois le petit spatumile dont ci est li forme:	If the baby comes out naturally from the head and the mother labors heavily, and the strength of her veins is weak, then she should sit on a stool or be held by women; and prepare natural oils such as fenugreek to cook, and then put it between her thighs the small suppository of this shape:
et fende la secondine, et cope a son ungle tant que li moistors qui est ens corre fuers; et preint lou ventre de la femme tant que li enfes dessende, et s’il ne dessent, si covient clisterizer la femme de muscillaige de fenugrec avec oile de sisament; puis la fai preindre et esternuer de condisi, et tien sa bouche et son neis une houre: si istra maintenant l’enfes.	 And cleaves the second bone, and wraps it in a sponge as long as the moisture that is within hurries forth; then squeezes the woman's belly until childbirth descends, and if not delivered, one must enema the woman with muscatel wine made from fenugreek oil: then press her and induce vomiting for an hour: now deliver the child.

And if the hands are stretched out too much, you must gently and gradually reset them; if they cannot be reinserted, place a stool under her feet, lift the legs upwards; then stand the stool on the ground and support the woman so she does not strain while standing; if the hands still cannot be reinserted and the child is dead, clasp the hands with the cord previously placed in front, extract the child, and reset it evenly.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses piés	 From underneath the child's feet

des plaies	Of wounds
Nos avons jai dit en la division la cure des plaies; or vos dirons les cures de mains et de medicine, selonc l’acomplissement.	In the section on wound care that we have mentioned earlier; now we will discuss treatments for hands and general ailments according to their completion.
Je dis que les plaies sont diverses selonc ceu qu’elles sont faites, et selonc les leus ou les plaies sont faites, et de coi elles sont faites.	I say that wounds are varied depending on what they are caused by, and based on their origin or type of injury, and why they occur.
Les choses par coi plaies sont faites sont par gitement de piere, et taille d’espee et de couteil, ou de lance ou de fust ou de siette, ou de semblans choses; ou que sont faites selonc les leus dou cors, si com plaie que chiet sus le col, ou sus le chief, ou le peis, ou le ventre, ou le foie, et semblans membres; et je vos dirai la cure de chescune plaie, et encomencerai as plaies dou chief simples, car li remenbrance venra en son chapistre.	 Things by which wounds are made are from piercing of stones, and cutting with swords and axes, or lances or clubs or arrows, or similar things; or those that occur according to the nature of the body, such as a wound that bleeds from the neck, or the head, or the thigh, or the abdomen, or liver, and similar limbs; and I will tell you the cure for each wound, beginning with simple wounds of the head, for memory will come in its place.
Je dis que quant simple plaie vient ou chief, et li os n’est brisiez, si pren garde se c’est de gitement de piere ou de semblans choses, et li cuir est toutevoie rompus et est li plaie grans, et tu doutes levement d’aposteme chaut: si le fai tantost sainier de la cephalique meismement s’il vient poc de sanc de la plaie, et soit li sainie au contraire de la partie navree; et eschuisse li malaides repletion de vin et de viandes grosses. Et s’il ne vuet sainier, si soit amenuisie sa viande, et ne boive point de vin, ne ne menjuce point de char; et met sor la plaie, se apostemes chaus i vient, coton moilliet en oile roset soulement, ou en vin stiptice; et s’il n’i a aposteme chaut, si met sus la plaie, s’elle est fresche a tout son sanc, et elle n’est muee par l’air, poudre, que je dirai un poc ci aprés; et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucuns oignemens, tant qu’il soit sanez. dou derrompement dou ventre	The second disruption of the belly
Li derompemens dou ventre est grans et moiens et petis; de la grant plaie saut aucune fois li intestine, ou li ners des intestines, par coi li intromission d’aus; et li costure est plus malaisie, et aucune fois vaut pis li petite plaie que li grans, por ceu c’on remet plus a poinnes les intestines en, s’on ne les i remet de chaut en chaut; por ce que li intestine enflent tantost qu’il sentent le froit, si rentrent plus a poinnes, et por ceu vaut mues li moieinne plaie, por ceu c’on ramoine mues l’intestine a son leu que as autres II Et saiches que li routure dou ventre est selonc IIII manieres: les II costures communes avienent en la costure dou ventre, et li costure des autres plaies dou cors et II autres costures propres sont communes as autres plaies; et toutevoie elles sont plus propres avec la costure dou ventre, et je dirai une chescune et declairerai.	 The collapses of the belly are large and medium-sized and small; from a great wound never once do the intestines fall or their nerves, allowing for entry; and suturing is more difficult, and it's worse with a smaller wound than a larger one because when resetting the intestines there are fewer pulls needed if not done very hot to hot; because the intestines swell almost immediately upon feeling cold, they retract more easily, and hence why a minor injury is moved more than a major one as you suture them in place. And know that the treatment of the belly wound occurs in four ways: the common stitches happen on the abdomabdomen wound, and the stitches from other body injuries and two specific types are common with other wounds; however, they're always more appropriate for the abdominal wound, and I will explain each one and declare.
Je di que quant li plaie est petite, et aucune chose de l’intestine ist fuer, et griés chose est dou remettre, ceu est par l’une des II manieres: ou por la petitece de la plaie, si com nos avons dit, ou por ce que li intestine est enflez por le froit.	 When the wound is small and nothing of the intestines is torn, there are few things to be put back in place, either by the nature of the wound as we have said, or because the intestines are swollen due to cold.
Et quant il est frois, eschaufez lou en teil maniere: moillie une esponge ou I mol drapeil en aigue tede soulement, ou tu cuis en aigue squinant et cipre et spique, et arose l’intestine tant que li enfleure soit ostee; et aucune fois fait ce vins restraingnans, et est muedre que awe soule por desenfler.	 And when it is cold, warm the area in one way: moisten an absorbent sponge or use wet linen lightly, or immerse in hot water and soap and salt, and raise the intestine until swelling is reduced; do not make this too restrictive, as loosening helps to reduce swelling.
Et quant tu vois l’enfleure departir, si amoiste l’intestine d’aigue ou altee et malves soient cuites, car par ceu est aligie li entree a poc de chose; et s’il n’i puet entrer, si fent un poc la plaie a l’estrument de coi on cope les emorroydes; et li premiere cure est muedre que li taille, que nus n’i doit taillier sens grant necessiteit n’i ait; et c’est li estrumens por le fendre: si trenche dedens en la corbeure et defuer non, et vez ci la forme:	 And when the swelling subsides, moisten the intortine with hot or cold water, as this helps to dilate the opening; and if nothing can pass through, gently create a hole using an instrument for treating bunions; the first treatment is to enlarge the incision without great necessity or need, which serves as dilation: cutting inside in the corrugated area but not too deep, observing its shape.
Et quant li plaie est enlargie, et li intestine saut fuer, si le remet arer selonc la forme naturel en son leu propre, se tu en as pooir, car ce vaut mues.	 When the wound is expanded and the intestines burst outward, if you can put them back in their natural place properly, do so if possible, because it will heal.
Quant li plaie est large, et elle est en la partie desoz lou ventre, si covient que tu faices gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et met ses jambes plus haut que son chief; et s’elle est en la partie desoz le ventre, si met le chief et le pis plus haut que les parties desoz, et ausi se li routure dou ventre est en l’une des II parties si met t’entente en ceu que li partie navree soit plus haute que li autre; et ensi covient amenistrer ceu que je dis en plaies grans et moienes.	 When the wound is large and it's located below the belly, it's appropriate to lay the patient on their back with legs raised higher than the head; and if it's under the belly, raise the head and hips higher than that area, and similarly for stitching around the belly in either of the two areas, make sure the sewn part is raised higher. That's how you should treat large and medium-sized wounds as I have described.
Es plaies petites met ceu que t’est apparilliet, puis aies entre tes mains I ministre pitous ki teigne toute la routure a sa main, et assemble les levres; et c’est la maniere commune de costures, et est que tu preignes une aguille ou plusors, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce de la plaie, puis laisse des le chief de la plaie I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une aguille ou il ait I boin fil fort; et perce les II chiés dou cuir avec les II chiés dou siphac, qui est desoz le cuir dedens, tant que tu la faices percier de celle partie, et assemble les II chief dou siphac les IIII ensamble; puis l’estrain d’un fil double entor l’aguille de II pars, puis assemble les II chiés de la plaie avenanment, et puis laisse I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une autre aguille; puis la lie dou fil si com tu as fait la premiere aguille, et ne cesser de ceu faire selonc ceu que tu as mestier des aguilles, tant que toute li plaie soit restrainte; et soient les aguilles moienes, entre subtilz et grosses, car les aguilles subtilz copent toute la char, et les trop grosses si ne pueent mie bien entrer: por ceu covient qu’elles soient moienes; et ne covient mie bouter les aguilles trop au defuer de la char et dou cuir, k’elles ne copent et oevrent la plaie devant la soudure; et puis cope les chiés des aguilles, qu’elles ne blecent lou malaide au dormir, et i met tentes ou drapelz au chiés des aguilles por mues tenir, et les laisse tant que li plaie soit soudee; et ceste maniere de costure as aguilles est plus covenauble en petites plaies, car il i soffist une aguille ou II Li seconde costure si est commune, et est que tu assemble les II chiés dou cuir et les II chiés dou syfac ensamble a une aguille ou il ait I fort fil moien; et quant tu avras perciez ces chiez toz IIII ensamble, si ramoinne l’aguille a la partie ou tu as encomenciet, en la maniere c’on cout les dras; et met d’espaice entre chescune costure la grossece d’un menor doi; ceste costure sevent li home, et je cousi une plaie c’uns hons avoit ou ventre, qui estoit navrez d’un coutel, et estoit li plaie plus d’une palme de grant, et issoit des intestines bien II palmes de grant, et estoit li plaie enmi le ventre.	 For small wounds, prepare as follows: have two ministers who can sew the edges together; it's common practice for sutures and depending on the size of the wound, you will need a certain number of stitches. Leave space from the head of the wound with I inch between each stitch, using an appropriate needle or multiple ones; then pierce both edges of the skin with the same thickness as those beneath the skin and sew them together until complete, pulling double thread through the needle's eye. For sutures that are more than one palm wide, leave space between each stitch in such a way you have assembled all parts; then pull a double thread around two needles, and promptly stitch the wound edges as soon as you finish with one needle. Continue this until the entire wound is closed with sutures of medium thickness—neither too fine nor too coarse, as very fine ones might not penetrate properly, while too coarse may not close well; hence they should be of medium thickeinse: do not place stitches too far from the wound and skin surface that they don't adequately seal or support it. Then tie off each suture so as to avoid discomfort when the patient sleeps, cover with gauze or fabric over the sutures for comfort until fully healed; this method using medium-thickness sutures is better suited for small wounds. Another common way of stitching involves connecting both sides of the skin and underlying tissue to a single needle with medium thread thickness—after piercing all four layers together, reinsert the needle back at its starting point following how fabrics are sewn; leave space between each suture equal to one minor unit. This is known as stitching for people; I've performed this on a man whose abdomen was injured by a knife wound measuring more than one palm in width, and the intestines were protruded outward about two palms wide, with the injury located within his belly.
Je li ramenai l’intestine puis k’il ot esteit XXIIII houres fuer, et fut li plaie soudee jusc’a XV jors, et le curai, et fut sanez.	 I returned his intestines since it had been fourteen hours, and the wound was sutured up to fifteen days, and I treated him, and he recovered.
Et li mire l’avoient jugiet qu’il morroit, et ce fut miracle; et ne le curai mie d’oignement, car je estoie en I leu ou on n’en trovoit point, ne nule medicines; et metoie sens plus sus la plaie coton viel II fois le jor, et le lavoie d’aigue de miel tant qu’il fut sanez.	 And the master thought he would die, and it was a miracle; I did not treat him with ointment as there were none to be found in this place or any medicines; instead, I placed twice-aged cotton over the wound each day, and bathed it with honey water until he recovered.
Or vos dirai les II propres manieres de cousture: pren l’aguille, et la boute des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens; quant elle a perciet le keur de droit en droit, si lai le chief dou siphac ou cousteit ou tu as bouteit l’aguille, et la fai percier d’autre part des la partie dedens jusc’a celi defuer; et li entendemens de ceste costure si est que tu cous ausi com li peletier font les pelz, et que tu laisses une fois le syfac d’une part, et le reprent d’autre, tant que li costure soit toute acomplie.	 Now I shall tell you the two proper ways of stitching: take the needle and thread it through to the depth just mentioned; when it pierces the flesh straight from left to right, remove the suture or where you inserted the needle, and then thread it back from within outward as far as specified; thus, the concept of this suturing is like that of a tailor making seams, leaving once the skin unstitched on one side and re-threading from another until the stitching is complete.
Li seconde maniere de costure, que Galiens dist proprement, si est si com aucun font, qui assemblent les II parties ensamble naturelment, et apploient l’un des chief dou syfac a l’autre chief, en teil maniere: fiche une aguille ou chief dou mirach prochiene, et fai percier celui leu soulement, et laisse les II chiés dou syfac; puis torne l’aguille, et la fai percier des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, as II chiés dou syfac; puis fai percier l’un et l’autre des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, en II autres chiés dou mirach que sont on l’autre costeit; et c’est li muedre maniere de costure et li plus commune.	 The second manner of suture, as Galien describes it properly, is such that anyone does, joining the two parts together naturally and placing one end of the membrane to the other, in this way: insert a needle or thread next to the mucous membrane, make an incision at only that location, leaving both ends of the membrane; then turn the needle, and make another incision from the part forward until reaching inside where there are two more ends of the mucous membrane; then pierce one and the other up to the part forward in two additional places of the membrane which are on opposite sides. This is the manner of suturing most commonly used.
Galiens si dist ceste parolle, et aucun le tesmoignent, c’on doit coudre le ventre a II aguilles, ou il ait fil en chescune; et doit on bouter l’une aguille d’une part, et l’autre d’autre, en la maniere de ces qui cousent corroies; et saiches que quant li routure est enmi lou ventre, si est li cousture plus griez que des autres leus dou ventre.	 Galen states this word and no one denies it, that the belly should be sewn with two needles, each having thread; and place one needle on one side, and the other on the opposite side, in the manner of those who sew straps; so that when there is a rupture within the belly, then this suture is more challenging than others involving parts of the belly.
Li jugemens de la plaie si est telz com li jugemens des autres plaies: et est que quant tu trueves la plaie fresche a tout son sanc, ainsois que li ars l’ait muee, si remet arer l’intestine, et lou cout; puis met sus la poudre enjanrant char, et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucun oignement que soit present, tant que li plaie bowe; et chicent li fil, et soient soudez li sifac, et li mirach; puis cure la plaie si com les autres, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu n’as medicines, si met sus, tantost qu’ele comance a giter bowe, coton viel, et le remue II fois le jor tant k’il soit sanez.	 The assessment of the wound is such as with other wounds: and it is that when you find the fresh wound fully bleeding, just as if the arrow had moved it, reset the intestines and the belly; then apply powdered charcoal ointment, and if the arrow has moved, apply any present poultice until the wound hardens; trim the thread, tie securely with silk and linen; then treat the wound as others, until it is sound; and if you have no medicines, apply a ball of cotton at first when it begins to bleed lightly, two times a day until it heals.
Car tu n’as mestier d’autre medicine en plusors dispositions cant les plaies sont simples; et se tu doutes que li plaie ne faice communiteit as membres principelz, si covient ke tu moilles lainne legiere en oile de tempree chalor, ou en oile roset, et la met entor les angres, et desoz les asselles; et s’il sent dolor ou porriture en bouelz, et maintes fois avient, si les clisterize de vin noir tede, et meismement se li porriture vient jusc’a l’intestine; et le perce dedens, et saiches que quant c’est li gros intestines, si est plus legier a saner que li petis.	 You don't need any other medicine in certain cases where wounds are simple; and if you doubt that the wound affects the principal limbs, then you should gently rub linen with lukew groggy oil or rose oil between your hands, and place it near the joints and under the elbows; and if they feel pain or swelling in the belly, which happens often, then administer a black wine enema, especially if the swelling reaches up to the intestines; and probe inside, noting that when it is the large intestine, it is easier to heal than the small one.
Li intestine qui est apelez «jeun» ne puet saner quant il est navrez, et c’est por la planteit des voinnes que i sont, et por la subtiliteit de tout le cors, et l’aprochement de sa nature des ners.	 The intestine called "jejunum" cannot heal when it is afflicted, and this is because of the poison from wounds that are present, and due to the subtlety of the entire body and its proximity to the nerves.
Et si li zirbe saut de la plaie, si le remet arrier ausi com l’intestine, tandis qu’il est fres; et s’il est vielz et devenus vers ou noir, si covient que tu lies le leu qui est noir, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, car il i a voinnes et arteres; puis cope ceu qui est entre le liien, et met les II chiés pendans des la partie desoz la plaie jusque defuer por aligier l’estraction quant li zirbes chiet, et li plaie bowe.	 If the sinew springs from the wound, reset it like an intestine while still fresh; if it is old and turned yellow or black, then remove the dark area to prevent bleeding due to veins and arteries; next bind what lies between the ligaments, and hang two heads of leeches from below the injury site until extraction when the sinew slips out, and the wound heals.
de la routure dou boueil	be it comes as f not cane them a lign bette a le :th d’s li;
Quant li intestine est rons, et li plaie est petite, si la puet on restorer en aucuns homes, por ceu que je vis que uns hons fut navrez ou ventre d’une lance; et estoit li plaie au destre de l’estomac, et fut envillie et devint fistule, et en issoit li egestion et li ventositez; je i mis cure selonc ceu que je poi, et ne cessai de subtilier tant qu’il fut sanez, et li leus soudez.	 When the intestine protrudes and the wound is small, it can be restored in certain cases as I have seen a man was stabbed with a lance; the wound was on the right side of the abdamen, becoming hollowed out and turning into a fistula causing egestion and flatulence; according to what I could do, I provided care and did not cease delicate procedures until healed, and the sinew closed.
Et quant je le vis souder, je doutai que li malaides n’eust mal en son ventre; et il n’i ot point de mal, mais demora en millors dispositions, et menjans et bevans; et dirent aucun experimentors que quant il a petite plaie en l’intestine, qu’il doit estre liiez en teil maniere: pren fremis a grans testes, puis assemble les levres de la plaie, et quant li fremis ait overte la bouche, si la met sus les II levres, si qu’elle estraigne sa bouche sus; et puis li cope la teste, et ce se tient si qu’il ne puet desliier, puis met I autre fremit aprés en celle maniere que devant, tant que li plaie soit toute porprise; et cout la plaie.	 When I saw it joined up, I doubted that the patient might have harm in his stomach; and there was no harm at all, but he remained in better conditions, eating and drinking; and some experimenters said that when there is a small wound inside the intestine, it should be treated this way: take frog's gall from large heads, then bring together the edges of the wound, and once the frog's gall has opened its mouth, place it over the two lips so that it stretches out; and then cover its head, ensuring it does not come apart, then put another frog's gall afterward in the same manner until the entire wound is closed; and heal the wound.
Cil chief si s’aerdent en l’intestine, et ne vient nulle nuisance au malaide, et se puet on liier l’intestine d’un fil subtil qui est copez de l’intestine d’une beste, en teil maniere: pren le chief de cest fil d’intestine que soit mout descharnez, et puis lie au chief de cest fil I fil de lin subtil tort, puis boute le fil en l’aguille, et en cout l’intestine, et le ramoinne en la routure; et ceste maniere de costure de fremis nen est fuers que selonc la voie de fiance et d’esperance; et se li plaie est grans et large, meismement quant elle est en l’un des grailes intestines, si n’i a engien ne santeit, fuer que subtiliteit.	 In the intestine, it swells without harm to the patient, and you can tie the intestine with a fine thread cut from the intestine of an animal: take the end of this thread of intestine that is quite cleaned, then bind it to the end of a subtle linen thread, put the thread through the needle, and sew the intestine in such a manner; this method of suturing from within is no further than according to trust and hope; and if the wound is large and wide, especially when it's in one of the corners of the intestines, there is no remedy or health, save for subtlety.
de fistule ou qu’ele soit	of a fistula or if it exists
Saiches que toute plaie ou aposteme, quant il enveillist, si est apelee universement «fistule», et meismement quant elle est chevee et rent bowe.	 Every wound or abscess, when it ages, is generally called "fistula," especially if it oozes and heals with scars.
Et fistule est selonc la verteit nodation fautree dure et blainche, ou on ne sent dolor, et est ausi chevee com li penne d’un oiseil; et aucune fois en saut clere bowe, et autre fois espesse; aucune fois poc, et autre fois assez; et je en ai jai parleit en la division des plaies, que toute plaie que n’est sanee, et il n’i a char, ce n’est fuers que par une des VIIII causes: c’est a savoir, par la petitece dou sanc ou cors; ou por sa malice; ou por ceu qu’il i a char dure dedens, et sus les levres, que n’i laisse naistre char; ou il i a trop de bowe; ou li leus est porris, et li matiere est de male qualiteit; ou li medicine n’est mie bone en la cure; ou por ceu que li corruption est maniere de pestilence; ou por la proprieteit en la region est tardive li digestion, et tarde li santeit, et enflee par nature; ou il i a voinnes ou os: et j’ai ja mostreit toutes ces causes, et les signes, et les cures de medicines en la division.	 A fistula is caused by improper blood flow and pus, without pain, and healing like the feathers of a bird; sometimes it weeps clear pus, other times thick; occasionally little, at other times enough; and I have discussed in the section on wounds, that any unhealed wound does not close naturally, except due to one of the nine causes: namely, because of too much blood or body heat; or its inherent badness; or hardening inside with swelling above the edges preventing exudate from escaping; or excessive pus; or the flesh being rotten and of poor quality; or inappropriate medication for treatment; or due to decay as a form of plague; or because digestion is slow, recovery is delayed by nature; or presence of tumors or bone fragments: and I have already shown all these causes, their signs, and remedies using medicines.
Or covient que je te faice a savoir la cure de fistule qui est faite par oevre de mains.	Or it is necessary for me to inform you about the treatment of an abscess made by handwork.
Saiches que fistule avient en tous membres dou cors; car il i a fistules que vienent as grans voines, et as arteres, et as ners, ou au syfac, ou a l’intestine, ou a la vessie, ou a aucunes des costes, ou a l’espinee dou dos, ou a aucune jointe des mains ou des piez; et si a teil que vient a la proprieteit dou membre principeil, et as semblans leus.	 Fistulas occur in all members of the body; for there are fistules that arise from great veins and arteries, and nerves, or at the liver, or intestine, or bladder, or to certain ribs, or the spine of the back, or any joint of hands or feet; and they also occur in the principal member and its counterparts.
Et toutes les fistules que sont de ceste maniere sont de grief sanation, et n’i a fors que labour, et ignorance; et se il i a aucune fistule que ne veigne mie jusc’a leu que j’ai dit, et tu as fiance de la cure, et tu la vues conoistre, si pren une tente d’arain ou de fer, se li fistule est droite, si la quier; et se li fistule est torte, si la cerche d’une subtil tente de plonc, car li plons se ploie mues entor la tortuositeit; et se li fistule a mains pertus et tu ne la pues mie bien cerchier par tentes, si la clisterize par l’un des pertus, car la moistors si cort d’un pertus a autre, et la mundifie; puis la quier saigement a ton pooir, que tu conoisses s’il i a os ou nerf, et est chevee em parfont, et demande bien au malaide de la dolor qu’il sent au presser de ta main, et le leu ou il la sent; et quant tu savras vraiement le leu ou elle est, et s’elle est loing de jointure, ou de nerf, ou d’artere ou de voine, ou en aucuns des leus que je t’ai dit, si la cope selonc ceu que je t’ai dit, et oste fuer la fautreure et les chars corrumpues que sont dedens; et puis la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee, et se li fistule est bien parfonde de droit endroit, si covient que tu copes em parfont, tant com tu pues, puis i met tentes moillies en medicine ague, et les boute jusc’au chief de la fistule, tant que li medicine corrode la superfluiteit qui est demoree au fons; et puis i met oignemens enjanrans sainne char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez par ceu, si le cauterize si com nos avons dit, et se li os est corrompus de la fistule, si le cope.	 All such types of fistulas have a serious prognosis and only involve labor and ignorance; if there is any type of faster that does not reach the extent I mentioned, but you trust in its healing, and it appears to be healed, then take an awning made of wicker or iron, depending on whether the fistula is straight or twisted, as the planks can bend around a subtle tension; if the fistula has exposed openings that cannot be accurately examined using tenting techniques, use a clisterization from one of its openings to cleanse it because moisture dissipates quickly from one opening to another and cleanses it. Then firmly grasp it with your strength as you can determine if there is bone or nerve, and whether it swells completely; ask the patient about the pain they feel when pressed by your hand, and where it is felt; once you have accurately identified its location, and if it is far from a joint, nerve, artery, vein, or any of the locations I mentioned, then treat according to what I've said, removing impurities within. Then continue curing until fully healed, and if the fistula has penetrated deeply in its proper location, you should cauterize it entirely where possible, after which apply bandages soaked with medicinal ague up to the head of the fistule, as long as they corrode the superfluity at the bottom; then apply healing balm ointments until fully healed. If not by this means, cauterize it as we have said, and if bone is corrupted within the fistula, excise it.
Se voinne ou ners ne te greve ou membres principelz, si com nos avons dit; et se li os est descovers, et il i a corruption et noiror, si lou reis tant que li corruption soit toute ostee, puis le cure de choses enjanrans char tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez, et rent bowe si com devant, saiches que tu n’es mie alez jusc’a font: si descuevre et quier tant que tu soies au fons, et oste toute la corruption, puis restore le leu; et s’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	 If veins or nerves are affected or principal limbs; as we have said; and if the bone is exposed, and there is decay and blackness, so rule until the decay has consumed all the bone, then treat various things gently until it becomes healthy; and if not healed, return to bowing as before, knowing you should not go near fire: expose and wait until reaching the bottom, remove all decay, then restore its place; and if thus it is made healthy, that's good.
Se ceu non, saiches que la corruption est trop en parfont, que tu n’i pues avenir; si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier a nature; et s’il i a i petit os corrumput, et tu le pues traire as tenailles, si l’estrai a I estrument covenauble a ceu, et s’il i a maint os, si les trai trestoz, ne n’en laissier nes un; et se li moistor te fait contraire, et il n’i a error ne paour, si cope et moistor et char, et delivre les os.	 If not, know that the decay is too extensive to approach; there is no other remedy than latchets of nature; and if there are small corrupted bones, you can extract them with pincers using a suitable instrument for such, and if there are many bangs, pull out all except one; and if moisture acts against it, and there is neither mistake nor fear, apply compresses, moisture, and heat, and free the bones.
Et se tu ne les pues oster a une houre, si met sus la plaie chose enjanrant porriture, et laisse tant que li leus soit porris entor les os, et adonc si avront plus legierement les os; et se c’est uns grans os, si com de jambe ou de cuisse, si reis tant soulement la corruption tant que li noiror soit toute ostee, puis restoure la plaie; et s’il en i a grant partie dou corrumput, et vient jusc’a mole de l’os; si le covient soier et coper tout jusc’a la corruption, et puis le cure tant qu’il soit soudez; et je te dirai d’une fistule qui avint I home en sa jambe, si que tu i preignes exemple et aide en ton ovraige.	 If you cannot remove them within an hour, apply something that causes putrefaction to the wound and leave it until the flesh is rotten around the bones; then the bones will be more easily released; and if it's a large bone like from the leg or thigh, completely cover the corruption until all the bone has decayed, then close the wound; and if there is a significant part of the bone affected by corruption, reaching nearly to the marrow, you must entirely encase it up to the point of corruption, then cure until solidified; and I will tell you about a fistula that occurred in one man's leg, from which you can take example and aid for your work.
Il fut I jovencelz entor XXX ans, qui ot une dolor en sa jambe d’une cause que vint dedens le cors, tant que les matieres vinrent a la jambe, et fut enflee d’un gros aposteme, et n’ot point de cause defuer por ovrir; mais li mire par lor folie ovrerent tant sus que li apostemes ovri, et en corroient mout de matieres, et devint fistule, et i vint mout de pertus que tuit gitoient bowe et moistor dou cors; et maint mire i mirent cure entor II ans, et n’i ot nul saige en l’art de mains, tant que je i fui apelez, et vi sa jambe et les medicines dont on le curoit, et ceu que corroit par les pertus a grant cors; et devenoit rouges li cors dou jouvenceil, et avoit color citrine.	 Once there was a young man of about thirty years old who had pain in his leg from a cause that came inside the body until substances reached the leg and fled from a large abscess, but without any apparent reason to open it; however, by their folly doctors worked so much on it that they opened the abscesses, and there were consumed many materials, which became fistulas, and there was excessive moisture in all parts of the body; several physicians attempted treatment for two years without any success in the art of healing by hands, until I was called upon, and saw his leg and the medicines with which they treated him, as well as what flowed through the fistulas to a large part of the body; consequently, the young man's body turned red, and it had a citrine color.
Je boutai une tente en l’un de ces pertus, et puis cerchai toz les pertus, et trovai que li uns venoit encontre l’autre de toutes les parties de la jambe.	 I erected a tent on one of these points, and then searched for all the points, finding that each comes in contact with the other from all parts of the leg.
Je me hastai donques, et copai en l’un des pertus tant que je descovri une partie de l’os, et le trovai corrumput et perciet, et venoit li corruption jusc’a l’os dedens; je soiai ceu qui m’aparissoit de l’os corrumput, et cuidai qu’il n’i eust autre corruption, fuer que celi que je ostai; et comensai a restourer la plaie de medicines sodans par lonc tens, et ne pot souder; et puis rencomensai, et descovri l’os si com devant, et trovai la corruption continuee en l’os, et la soiai, et puis l’ostai, et me penai de souder le leu; mais je ne pou tant que je copai entor une palme de l’os, et le traï fuer a tout son mole, puis le restourai de medicines; et il fut sanez et soudez hastanment, et ne covint plus rencomencier l’ovraige fors por la foibleté dou malaide, qui ne pooit soffrir, et por la paour de mort que je avoie de lui.	 Therefore I proceeded and cut into one of the points as far as I discovered a part of the bone, finding it corroded and pierced, with corrosion reaching to the inner bone; I perceived what seemed to be from the corroded bone, assuming there was no other corruption apart from that which I showed; so I began treating the wound with medicinal plasters over a long time, but could not sew it up; and then I resumed treatment, discovering the bone as before, finding continuous corrosion in the bebone, which I treated, and then removed it, and tried to suture at the location. However, I was unable to cut around the entire bone with just a span of my hand, causing the plaster to fail entirely; so I restored it again with medicines. It quickly healed and sewed up promptly, without having to restart treatment except due to the patient's weakness who could not bear it, and from fear of death that I had for him.
Car por l’evacuation sanglotoit sovent, mais il fut sanez entierement, et nasquit en leu de l’os une char dure, et fut de bone disposition et n’ot point de nuisement ne de contraire dou tout en tout, ne a l’aleir ne a venir.	 For the evacuation of blood often made him faint, but he recovered completely, and in place of the bone there grew a hard callus, which was well-formed and had no detriment or disadvantage at all, neither to walking nor coming.
Et se li os est brisiez en aucun leu dou cors, si le covient soier en ceste maniere: pren I liien, et l’estrain au chief de l’os qui apert, et comande aucun k’il l’estende en haut; et met I autre lien de lainne plus gros dou premier liien, et le lie sus la char qui est desor l’os, et estent le chief, si que tu traies la char corrumpue au desoz, et descuevre la char sus le leu ou tu vues soier, que li soie ne blece la char; et met I tison ou une tauble desoz l’os por mues coper la char corrumpue; et covient tant soier com on puet veoir et sentir la corruption, et soier ancor autre fois.	 And if the bone is broken in any part of the body, then it should be treated as follows: take a line, and straighten the head of the broken bone that protrudes, and command no one to move it upwards; and put another thicker piece of cloth on the first line, and tie it over the callus on the bone, and pull the ends so that you tear away the rotten callus from below, and expose the healthy callus at the place where you want to heal, ensuring that nothing touches the callus; and put a tine or a piece of wood under the bone to support the rotten callus; and it must be treated until one can see and feel the corruption has been removed, and then treat it again if necessary.
Et se li os est corrumpus, et n’apert mie, et li corruptions est en mileu ou en une partie, si descuevre la char toute; puis met I tison desoz, et puis soie des l’une partie a l’autre la corruption, et soit li soieure dou lonc de la corruption I poc, si com nos avons dit; et se li corruptions est en la jointure, si cope la jointure corrumpue, et soie l’os ou elle contient de l’autre part; et se li corruptions est en la continuation des II jointes, si n’i a autre angien que dou coper; et se li corruptions est ou poignil de la main, ou ou poignil dou piet, si est mout fort celle chose, mais toutevoie il covient que tu enquieres celle corrosion, coment elle t’apert; et la mundifie en toutes les manieres que tu pues, mais que li voine ou li nerf ne te faicent contraire; et saiches que li incisoire et les soies por coper ces os sont maintes, selonc l’assise des os et l’aparance d’ous, et lor grossece et lor subtiliteit, et lor grandor et lor petitece, et lor duresce; et por ceu covient il apareillier a chescune semblance d’ovraige son estrument; et saiches que l’uevre te moustrera l’estrument dont tu avras mestier, selonc la conissance de cest art, et le tesmoignaige des manieres des maladies; si porpense l’estrument dont tu as mestier selonc ceu qu’il le covient.	 If the bone is corrupted and does not open, and the corruption is in the midst or in a part, reveal the entire wound; then apply fire from above, and then proceed with heating from one part to another the corruption, and let it be longer than half of the length of the corruption as we have said; and if the corruption is at the joint, cut off the corrupted joint, and remove the bone or what contains it on the other side; and if the corruption is in the continuation of two joints, there is no other remedy than doubling up; and if the corruption is at the end of the hand or foot, that matter is very strong, but nevertheless one must investigate how that corrosion opens to you, clean it with all possible means without causing irritation to the vein or nerve; and know that incising instruments and probes for covering these bones are many, according to the position of the bones and their appearance, and their thickness and subtlety, their size and smallness, and hardness; therefore it must be equipped with an instrument suited to each kind of work. And know that the craft will show you which tool you need, in accordance with knowledge of this art, and the testimony of the ways diseases manifest themselves; so ponder upon the instrument needed according to what is fitting.
dou feu	If by fire
Li chiés porrissent ou par cause dedens, ou par cause defuer; et quant tu avras medicinee celle corrosion par la cure des medicines, et il ne profitent mie, si covient coper celui membre jusques au leu ou li corrosion vient, si que li malaides eschaipe par ceu de la mort, ou par la malice, qui est plus grans, de la defaute dou membre; et li signes si est que li membres devient noir, si qu’il semble qu’il soit ars dou feu, et porrist aprés la noiror, pues va celle corrosions de membre em membre, et prent par tout le cors; si te haste dou coper, et se c’est par la percussion d’aucunes venimouses bestes, si com scorpion de mer et wivre et semblans, se li corrosion est au chief dou doi, si le cope, et ne li doner mie espaice de venir jusc’a la main.	 The head may rot or perish due to internal causes, or lack thereof; and when you have administered the medicine for this decay through medicinal treatment, but they prove ineffective, then it is necessary to cover that limb up to where the decay occurs so that the patient escapes death's embrace or its greater harm from the member's deficiency; and signs are such that the limb turns black as if scorched by fire, followed by the blackness of rotting of limb to limb, taking over the entire body. Act quickly with covering; and if it is due to the sting of venomous creatures like sea scorpions, snakes, etc., and decay occurs at the head of the joints, cover up but do not give any space for it to reach the hand.
Et s’elle vient jusc’a la main, si la cope a la jointe, si que la corrosion ne viegne jusc’a bras; et s’elle vient au bras, si le cope au coute; et s’elle passe le coute, c’est li mors, et n’i vaut amenistremens fuers que li quantitez de sa vertut; et tot ensi fai quant li corrosion vient ou piet: s’elle vient en la premiere jointe, si la cope aprés l’autre jointe; et s’elle vient ou piet, si cope tout le piet; et s’elle monte en la jambe, si cope a la jointure dou genoil; et s’elle vient desus le genoil, si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier le malaide a mort; et li maniere dou coper ou dou soier le membre si est que tu le lie desus et desoz, et estende uns menistres l’un des liiens aval, et uns autres ministres l’autre liien amont, et tu dessevre la char qui est entre les II liiens a I spatumile large, tant que li os soit descovers; puis le cope ou soie, et met de chescune part I drapeil de lin, si que li soie ne touche le leu sain, et viegne au malaide autre lesion et aposteme chaus.	 If it reaches the hand, cover the joint, ensuring that corrosion does not reach the arm; and if it reaches the arm, cover the elbow; and if it passes the elcuote, there is death, with no remedy except in relation to its effectiveness; and thus, whenever corrosion occurs or strikes: if it reaches the first joint, then cover after the other joint; and if it strikes a limb, then cover the entire limb; and if it ascends to the leg, cover at the knee joint; and if it surpasses the knee, there is no other remedy than to make the patient faint; the manner of applying or removing bandages should be such that you bind above and below, extending a mittin between the straps on one side, and another mitten on the opposite strap, then untie the cord which lies between the two straps wide enough so that the bone is exposed; then apply the cast or bandage, and place linen strips from each side, ensuring that the bandage does not touch the healthy area, causing further injury to the patient.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient quant tu oevres, si cauterize le leu hastanment, ou tu met sus aucunes poudres restraignans; puis revien a ta medicine tant qu’elle soit acomplie, puis lie le membre navreit d’un liien covenauble, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et je te conterai k’il avint a I home en som piet: il li avint une noiror qui sembloit arsure de feu, et celle corrosion vint premier en son doi dou piet, tant qu’elle porprist tout le piet; et quant li hons vit la corrosion, si se hasta de coper le piet, et fut sanez; et lonc tens aprés li revint li corrosion ou doi de la main, et il vint a moi, et je li mis sus choses repercussives aprés la mundification dou cors, et ne pot cesser li corrosions; et il vot que je li copasse la main, et je ne vou, que je avoie esperance de repercuter la matiere; et doutai ausi que se je tailloie sa main, qu’il ne morist, car li vertus de l’ome estoit foible; et il se despera toz, et revint en sa terre, et se hasta de coper sa main, et fut sanez; et je n’ai ceu conteit fuers que por ceu c’on faice autreteil, s’on en a mestier.	 When the flow of blood changes while you work, promptly perform a cauterization at the site or apply certain restraining powders; then return to your medicine until it is completed, then bind the wounded limb with an obligatory bandage and treat it until healthy again; and I will tell you what happened to a man in deep sleep: a blackness resembling fire burned him first on his thumbs down to the fingers, spreading throughout the entire finger; when the man saw the corrosion, he cauterized the wound with copper and was healthy again; after many years it returned to his elbow, then came to me, and I applied things that cause reactions after body cleansing, but could not stop the corrosions; so I bandaged his hand, unsure if there was hope of spreading the material; also doubted whether cutting his hand would kill him, for the vitality of the man was weak; he became desperate and returned to his homeland, cauterizing his hand himself and recovered.
Aucune fois vient aposteme en leu charnut, et demore si longement qu’il fait grant assemblee de bowe; et puis ront et perce, et en saut li bowe, et demoure li leus vuis, ausi com uns vasselz; et li cuir qui est desus est ausi subtilz com I drapelz deliiez, et ne corront mie jusc’a l’os, ne jusc’au nerf, et telz maladie si est apelee «sain», et n’est mie apelee «fistule»; mais s’elle est si alongie qu’elle viegne jusc’a l’os em parfont, si est apelee «fistule»; et li cuire si est que tu cope celui cuir tout entor, et meismement quant il est subtilz, ausi com uns drapelz; et ne s’aert mie por sa corruption.	 At no time does an abscess come to a hardened state, and it lingers so long that it forms a large mass of pus; and then bursts and drains, and the fat flows out, and the eyelids remain swollen like lambskin; and the skin above is as subtle as cut cloth, not reaching even to the bone or nerve, thus these illnesses are called "healed", not "fistula"; but if it becomes so large that it reaches near the bone fully, then it is called a "faster". The flesh should be excised completely around that area of skin; especially when it's as delicate as cut cloth.
Et se tu as fiance que li cuirs s’aerde, et li corruption n’est mie en parfont, et li cuir est espés de char, si le cure de clistere ensi: regarde se li seins est grans, et li bowe qui en ist est de puant odor, adonques le clisterize de medicine egiptiaine qui est ensi faite: prenez aisil, et oile, et litargire, igalment, et metez cuire en I vassel au feu, tant que li medicine soit rouge, et deviegne ausi espesse com miel; et puis pren de ceu selonc ta necessiteit, et le font en aigue et en miel, et en clisterize lou sein, et estraint le pertus; et laisse la medicine ens par II houres, puis l’estrai en espreignant; fai ce mout de fois, tant que li seins soit mondefiiez, et soit ostee li puor; et aucune fois est clisterizeis d’aigue de cendres, quant ceste medicine n’est presens, et est que tu preignes cendres de fust de vigne, et giete aigue desus, puis la coule, et en clisterize, tant que tu saiches que li seins est bien mondez; et se li malaides ne le puet soffrir, ne la medicine egiptiaine ne l’aigue de cendres, si le clisterize d’aigue et de miel ou il ait un poc de litargire broiet; ou tu la clistirize de miel et de vin melleit, que li mielz ait proprieteit de mundifiier et de laver, et li vins fait aerdre le sain; et quant tu as ce fait, et tu as fiance que li seins est bien mundifiiez, si le clisterize de ceu que fait naistre char en li, et est que tu preignes emplaustre diafinit, et le font avec oile roset et en vin; ou tu le clisterize d’aucunes medicines et d’oignemens, dont j’ai dit les proprietez ou traitier des oignemens; et se li pertus dou sein est petis, et li cainne dou clistere n’i puet entrer, si l’eslarge d’un fer un poc, et met ens une tente de l’oignement egiptiein, ou oignement basilicon, tant k’il soit eslargiez; et se li plaie est trop large, si la cout et i laisse tant soulement I leu ou li clistere puisse entrer, et se li pertus que giete bowe est au desus, si le cope ou plus bas leu que i est.	 If you believe the skin is hardened and not entirely rotten, and the skin is thick like leather, then this cure of an enema: check if the chest is large, and the bow that lies therein is foul-smelling odor; thus, enema with Egyptian medicine prepared as follows: take ease, oil, and litargyrion equally, and cook in a vessel over fire until the medicine turns red and thickens like honey; then take of it according to your need, and mix with water and hunter, enema the chest, and strain out the excrement; leave the medicine within for two hours, then extract by squeezing; do this many times until the chest is restored and the pus comes out; at no time are you to use an enema of simply water from ashes, unless this Egyptian medicine is not present. Instead, take ash from grapevine wood, add water above it, then pour through, and for an enema until you know that the chest has been restored properly; if the patient cannot bear either the Egyptian medicine or the water of ashes, do an enema with water and honey mixed in a little amount of litargyrion. Alternatively, use millefiori wine and honey for this purpose, because honey cleanses and wine purifies blood; first, ensure that the chest is properly restored before using any medicine or technique to bring out secretions.
Car quant li bowe est en parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char; et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si appareille en tel maniere que li bowe corre au plus bas leu que i est, car quant li bowe est parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si apareille en teil maniere: que li bowe corre legierement aval, et n’i lassier rien de la bowe; et pren medicines consolidatives por mettre sor le sain, et estent sus I drapeil de lin que cuevre tout le sain; puis cope as forces endroit le pertus dou sein I poc plus large dou premier, pues estent oignement souef sus I autre drapel selonc la quantiteit dou pertus, et le met sus le pertus dou sain por aligier la bowe, et n’oster mie le grant drapeil fuers que aprés maint jor une fois; et celui qui est sor le pertus dou sein, oste sovent por oster la bowe, et saiches ceu que corra de la bowe, se c’est venin ou poc ou assez, ou digeste, ou indigeste; et pren warde se li patiens sent dolor ou nom, et s’il i a aposteme ou non, et quant ta medicine s’est en teil maniere estendue et tu vois la nature que saut sus le pertus dou sain, si saiches que li seins s’aert ja, et aproche li santez; et puis le deslie le matin, ou le tier jor, et quant tu delies la plaie, si chainge I autre drapeil, et renovele l’oignement.	 When the bow is fully formed, do not allow it to bend without covering its back; and if you cannot cover the chest from below as you see fit, adjust in such a manner that the bow points towards the lowest point where it can be found, for when the bow is fully formed, do not allow it to bend without covering its back and if you cannot cover the chebt from below as you see fit, adjust accordingly: so that the bow moves slightly downward, and nothing impedes the bow; and take consolidating medicines to put on the wound, and extend over a linen bandage that covers the entire area; then cover the wounded spot with strengthening forces using another cloth according to the amount of the puncture, and place it on the puncture in the chest to support the bow, and do not remove the large bandage until after many days once; and those who are under the punctured part of the chest often remove it to alleviate the bending of the bow, and know if anything flows from the bow, whether it's poison or a small amount or sufficient, digested or indigested; and take care if the patient feels pain or numbness, and if there is an abscess or not, and when your medicine has spread in such a way that you see the nature of what rises from under the puncture on the chest, you know that the chest will heal soon, and approach health; then release it in the morning or after three days, and when you open the wound, change to another cloth, and renew the ointment.
Et se li seins giete bowe indigeste aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie.	And if the breasts become badly bruised after many days, it is said that the breasts do not heal.
Et se venins subtilz cort aprés lonc tens, si ne te desperer mie de la santeit, car li santez aproche.	 And if you encounter subtle chords after long periods of time, do not despair over health, for healing is nearing.
Car il i a homes cui tarde enjanremens de char en ses plaies, et de ces que font le contraire; et se bowe indigeste saut dou sein aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie; et se li seins tarde d’aerdre, et est porloigniez, si ajoste medicines sechans moistes en substance et seches en vertut, si com oignement diafinit, car il i a grant partie de vitriole, et c’est li derriene medicine; pren oignement dyafinit, et le font avec oile roset, et l’arose de viel vin igal en substance; puis le confit et en use; et ceu meisme fait mielz cuit engroissiez, quant oignemens dyafinit n’est presens, ou tu pren mirre et aloen et encens, et le broie, et le poudre sus le miel quant il est sor le feu; et puis en glue I drapel, et l’estent sor le sein, et aucune fois i aministre on aristologe longe, et racines de lis celeste, qui est ausi com farine de veces et centoire; et en use de simples ou de compostes: broie les, et en fai poudre, et met sus le miel que j’ai dit, et en use; et se li cure est alongie, et n’est curez par ceste cure, adonc saiches que la corruptions est em parfont, et fait empression en l’os, ou as membres durs, ou as liemens; si le cure de la cure de fistule, si com nos avons dit ci devant.	 And there are those who delay healing in their wounds, and some do the opposite; if an indigestible swelling occurs within the breast after many days, know that the breasts will not enlarge much; if they delay from growing, it is due to prolonged neglect, so apply medicines made of moist substances with dry qualities as a finished ointcuits like diaphinites because there is a large component of vitriol in them, which are considered the last medicine. Take diafinites and mix them with rose oil; then blend it evenly with old wine in terms of substance but fresh in virtue; afterwards, heat it and apply it. The same can be done with honey-cooked fat, when diafinites are not available or present, take myrrh, aloes, and incense, grind them, and powder over the honey as you place it on the fire; then wrap in a piece of cloth and apply to the breast for no long time, without using aromatic ointments or treating with celestial lily roots, which are similar to fine flour or bran. Use simple or compound mixtures: grind them, make into powder, add honey as mentioned earlier, and use it; if the treatment is extensive but not cured by this method, know that corruption has set in deeply, pressing on bones, hardened members, or ligaments; then proceed with the treatment for fistulas as we have previously described.
de l’aposteme de l’ungle	Of the abscess of the nail
Panarice est un aposteme que naist desoz l’ungle dou pouchiet de la main, ou dou piet, ou par aventure naist en autres dois; et quant il est envielliez, et on n’i prent garde, si i vient I aposteme chaus, et corront et giete bowe tant qu’elle corront la racine de l’ungle, et par aventure la corront toute; et vient li corrosions jusc’a l’os, tant qu’il i vient dolor puant, et est li chiés dou doi larges, et est li color fuxe.	 A boil is an abscess that arises under the nail of the hand or foot, or sometimes occurs in other joints; and when it matures, and no precautions are taken, so comes about an abscess which expands, and runs and oozes pus until it reaches the root of the nail, and by chance may consume the entire nail; leading to bone erosions up to the bone, causing intense pain, with swollen joints, and discoloration.
Quant tu le cures si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu copes a i. fer toute la superfluiteit qui est demoree de l’ungle, puis cauterize la plaie aprés.	 If you treat it as we have described in the section, and if treatment does not help, then it is necessary to cut off all excess tissue associated with the nail, then cauterize the wound afterward.
Li cauteres est mout grans aide se li os est sains, et li ungle est sainne; et se li ungle apresse la char ens, et l’encomence a poindre, et la blece, si covient que tu mettes lou rait desoz l’ungle que point la char, et la boute en haut, et cope celi char subtilment et legierement, et met sus le remenant de la char medicines ardans et corrosives por oster tout; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	 The caustic is very helpful if the bone is healthy and the nail is uninfected; and if the nail touches the skin, begins to hurt, and swells, then you must place a splint underneath the nail so it does not press against the skin, lift it upwards, and delicately remove the subtle tissue, and apply upon the remainder medicines that burn and are corrosive to eliminate all; then treat with ointments until they are healed.
Et se li corrosion est en l’os, si le cope, et trai fuer, car tant com li os corrumpus i est, si ne puet saner; et se tu vois le doi corrumpre, si le cope en I des nous si com il est devant dit, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il est ferus, et boutez, et il sent grant dolor, si covient que tu le sainnes premier; puis cope l’ungle dou spatumile agut en taillant de travers desus, et warde que li taille ne viegne jusc’a la char qui est desoz l’ungle, car li malaides sentiroit trop grant dolor; et s’il avient, si met chose sus qui apaise.	 And if the corrosion is in the bone, remove it and treat severely, as much as the bone corrupts, it cannot heal; and if you see the joint deteriorating, remove it as previously mentioned, then treat until it is healed; if it becomes severe, boils, and causes great pain, first alleviate the pain; then cut the nail with a small saw across from below, but be careful that the cut does not reach the skin beneath the nail, for the patient would feel too much pain; and if this occurs, apply something to soothe.
la dolor dou sourdoit de la main	The pain of soreness arises from the hand
Li dois ajostez qui naist en mains d’aucuns homes par aventure est toz charnus, et par aventure i a teil ou il a osses, et aucune fois i a ungle, et aucun d’aus naissent en la racine de la jointure, ou li naissance est en aucuns nous des dois.	 The dislocations that occur in the shoulders of some men by chance are all fleshly, and sometimes they have bones, and at other times there is no knuckle, and none of them grow in the root of the joint where the growth occurs in certain cases.
Cil qui naist en aucune nout dou doi ne se muet, et cil qui naist a la jointure dou doi, par aventure se muet; la taille de celui qui est charnus si est legiere, en teil maniere: taille le en sa racine d’un large spatumile.	 The one that occurs in any of our shoulder does not move, and the one that occurs at the joint of the shoulder sometimes moves; the stature of the fleshly ones is somewhat lightweight: lengthen it at its root with a wide span.
Cil qui naist en la racine de la jointure si est grief a curer: si te tien dou coper.	Those who are born at the root of the joint are more difficult to treat: take hold with your spatula.
En celui qui naist ou doit au derrien nout, si covient que tu copes premier la char reondement jusc’a l’os, puis cope l’os a une soie convenable a ceu, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	 In the one that occurs or forms on our next shoulder, it is necessary to first remove the roundness up to the bone, then cut the bone with an appropriate saw, and heal until it is sound.
Li soudemens que vient as dois ensamble vient par naissance, ou par soudement de plaie, ou par arsure de feu, ou par semblans choses.	The tendency that comes with age may arise from birth, or by sudden wound healing, or by scalding with fire, or similar causes.
