And when you have completed your work, take two strips of hazelwood that encircle the leg from one end to another, and are as long as the leg from knee to ankle; then wrap each in turns with a band above and below, tying them tightly together so the leg cannot lean left or right, which is good; and no one administers any other movement of the leg if it's made of wood, and they place the leg for protection from movement, properly done at the break where there is a wound; and move each day the leg to see if there are pus or any other accident; treat as long as it remains healthy.
de la brisure des os dou piet	From the fracture of the bone of the foot
A la cheville ne vient point de brisure, mais as os dou piet vient aucune fois brisure et as dois poc, et n’i avient fuer que quassure em plusor dispositions.	At the ankle there is no fracture, but at the foot's bone a break occurs and in the toes, with no injury that causes discomfort or certain conditions.
Et s’il avient as os dou piet brisure, et tu vois ces os sormonter l’un l’autre, si mette si malaides som piet sus la terre, ausi com s’il voloit aler, et puis met maintenant ton piet sus lou sien, lai ou li os sont levez, puis le presse tant k’il reveignent en lor leus; puis met l’emplaustre et estoupes sus, et met desoz lou ventre dou piet une petite tauble a .ij. chiés plains, puis l’estraint au piet avenanment, puis que tu as envoloupez drapelz entor, et autres choses dont tu as mestier.	And if there is a break in the foot bone and you see these bones protruding on each other, place your maladies so that the foot touches the ground just like it would walk, then place your own foot under theirs where the bones are elevated, then press until they return to their places; then apply the plaster and bandage around it, and put a small pincers with two flat points under the belly of the affected foot, then stretch it back to its normal position, after which you have wrapped cloths around, and other things as needed.
Et quant .iij. jors ou .iiij. seront passez, si deslie lou liien, car tu troveras les os igalz, soient brisiez, soient desaluez.	And when three or four days have passed, release the ligament because you will find the bones even, broken or dislocated.
Et s’il i a aucuns des dois brisiez, si les restoure, si com nos avons dit as dois de la main; puis met au doi brisiet une estele selonc la longesce dou doi, et soit un poc plus large, puis met desoz le piet celle tauble que j’ai dit, et l’estrain avenanment; et s’il en i a .ij. ou .iij., ou plus, brisiez, si met sus chescun doi une estele selonc sa quantiteit, envoloupee en .i. drapeil de lin, et estraint la tauble desoz lou piet; et soit estans sus lou chief de la tauble defuer lou ventre dou piet, si qu’il le teigne bien.	If there are any broken bones, repair them as we have said for the hand of a man; then place on the broken bone a splint according to its length and width, and place beneath the foot the table I mentioned earlier, and secure it quickly; and if there are two or three, or more, breakages, place on each bone a splint according to its amount, wrapped in one linen cloth, and attach the table beneath the leg so that they rest above the belly of the leg well.
Et covient que tu n’oblier mie les autres choses que j’ai dit as autres briseures, des que nos avons dit; et secor chescun accident si com il covient.	And it is necessary that you do not forget the other things I have said about other fractures, as we have mentioned; and treat each injury as it should be done.
de la brisure de l’os dou poignil	Regarding the breakage of the bone in the finger
Quant li os de la nature la femme est brisiez, si la fai seoir enlargie, puis l’encline a la partie dou dos, et soit tenue par derrier; puis emplisse li baile la nature de la malaide de couton, et en i mette ausi gros com I sto; puis deboute la femme, et lieve lou dos poc et poc, et adonques saut li coton, tant qu’il vient a l’entree de la nature, et revient li os avec lou sto; et quant elle vuet pissier, si oste lou coton, et quant elle a pissiet, se li remette, et ensi faice VII jors ou entor: si sera restoree li brisure, et se tu vues, pren une vessie de berbis, et lie au pertus une cainne, et boute toute la vessie en la nature; puis soffle en la cainne forment, tant que li vessie soit enflee dedens: la nature si revenra li brisure; puis soit emplie de coton, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 When the bone of a woman is broken and she must sit for an extended period, tilt her towards the less painful side, and support from behind; then fill the nature with linen cloth soaked in warm water according to its bulk; have her stand up gradually and slowly, and when possible, gently pull the linen out until it reaches the opening of the nature (vagina), and restores the bone fragment along with it. When she needs to urinate, remove the cotton, and once done, let it return to its place; continue this process for 7 days or so: if properly executed, the fracture will be restored. If you wish to ensure proper healing, take a goat bladder, tie a thread at one end, and fill it with warm water from the other side. Blow air into the tube until the bladader is filled; then let the nature return the broken bone. Fill it again with cotton and leave it like this for several days until healed.
Et quant li os dou poignil de l’ome est brisiez, ou de la femme, si le restoure ensi com nos avons dit en l’os de la hainche; et ne sont mie occultees ces briseures prochienes a celui qui i met son estude et son us, et entent mon livre.	 And when the bone of the arm's elbow is broken, or in women, restore it as we have said for the thighbone; and these fractures are not hidden from those who apply their study and work to this book.
Car li brisure li signifie em plusors dispositions la droite voie de la restauration: enten le donques.	 For the broken bone indicates various approaches for restoration: therefore, firstly.
En la verge, quant elle est brisie, pren une gorge d’oie et i boute la verge; puis envoloupe drapelz entor, et le laisse .iij. jors ou enqui entor, et il sera sanez hastanment.	When it should be done thus and in the brisure de l’oeu, que li les mete, tetre mout estent orle la haus, qui nes. Et quant elle vient ou ne pelez en entour, et le plix: soi sene au plusors; se pren, et les cholez la brisure de l'est que il rite.
de brisure avec plaie	Of fracture with wound
Il covient a celui qui a brisure avec plaie, meismement s’elle est grans, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire ou semblant, qu’il soit sainiez maintenant, si que les sainies que nos avons dit le tesmoignent.	It is necessary for those with a fracture and wound, especially if it is as large as the hip or shoulder bone or similar, to be well bandaged now, so that the bandages we have mentioned prove effective.
Et se li plaie saine, si la restainche de vitriole, se tu n’as autre chose, puis rencomence a restorer la briseure en cele meisme houre, ou celui jor, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the wound is healthy but has been touched by vitriol, if you have nothing else, then begin to reset the fracture again at that same hour or day, unless an abscess develops.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si laisse la restauration jusc’a nuevime jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et n’i touchier ne au tier jor ne au quart, car tu i feroies venir malvais accident.	they; s the t 0 :l* (do not quite, it: m one of the same.
Et se li os brisiez est aparans sus lou keur descovert, si covient que tu lou mettes a point legierement a tes mains, a extension petite.	And if the broken bone is visible above the joint, it should be carefully straightened slightly with your hands in small extensions.
Et se li extensions ne t’est apareillie por mettre igal a tes mains, si le ramoine a cest estrument qui est de fer, qui a .vij. dois ou .viij. de lonc, et li largesce est selonc la quantiteit de la plaie; et por ceu est mestier au mire qu’il empreigne .iii. ou iiij., selonc ceu qu’il en ait mestier en chescune cure de briseure; et soit rons et un poc gros, k’il ne ploie mie a la compression sus lou membre a ton ovraige, et soit agus devant, et gros des le mileu en avant, ensi:	And if the extensions do not allow you to adjust evenly with your hands, use this instrument made of iron, which has seven or six hooks and its width according to the amount of injury; thus it is necessary for the master that he grips three or four (hooks), depending on how much he needs in each fracture treatment; be round and slightly thick so that it does not bend under pressure on the limb during your work, with a large part forward:
Et est apelez «palainche», por coi il covient que li chiés corbes soit mis sus lou chief de l’os apparent; et le boute a une fois, tant k’il reviegne, et soit igalz l’un encontre l’autre.	 And it is called "palanching," so the head of the clavicle must be placed over the visible part of the bone; and then gently tapped until they are evenly aligned with each other.
Et se li brisure est subtilz, et li estrumens ne puet bien prendre l’os, si covient que tu copes lou chief de l’os, tant que li estrumens en ait possance.	 And if the break is subtle, and muscles cannot properly grip the bone, then it is necessary to cut off the head of the clavicle until the muscles have space.
Et se tu ne pues ramener l’os, si com nos avons dit, si lou cope d’un estrument covenable a ceu, ou incisoire ou soieure, a ton pooir; puis reis ceu qui est demorez en l’os d’aspreteit et de menues escorces.	If you cannot bring back the bone as we have said, with an instrument suitable for this purpose, either cutting or smoothening to your ability; then remove that which is lodged in the sharp and hard splinters of bone.
Et quant li os est ramenez, et li malaides sent grant dolor aprés, saiches qu’il n’est mie en son leu natureil.	 And when the bone is returned, and the patient feels great pain afterwards, know that it is not in its natural place.
Si fai tant qu’il soit en son leu, puis moille I drapeil en vin stiptique noir, et proprement se c’est en esteit; et ne mettre mie sus la plaie cerote ne autre chose ou il ait oile, qu’il n’i faice venir porriture et corruption; puis aministre esteles quant tu as restoreit l’os, et laisse la plaie descoverte, et cope la coverture tout entor, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et te done bien en garde que li plaie ne soit estrainte avec la brisure; et maintes fois ont ce fait li fol mire, et ont fait venir sus le malaide ou mort ou corrodent aucune fois; et soit li estrignemens plus molz et plus souef des autres brisures.	 If it is possible to place the bone correctly and then apply a black ointment mixed with vinegar, ensuring proper application; do not put any cerot or other substances on the wound that may cause rot and decay; once you have restored the bone and left the wound uncovered, wrap the entire area according to the size of the wound, taking care to avoid straining the wound with movement; many times, wise men have done this, bringing about healing or death in various cases. The tension should be gentler and more flexible than other fractures.
Et se li plaie est male ou grans, et tu doutes que mavais accidens n’i veigne, si com nos avons dit, et tu trueves dolor au leu, si n’i covient mie mettre sus esteles; mais envoloupe entor, en leu d’esteles, drapelz durs, et les lie.	 And if the wound is large or bad, and you suspect that no incident has occurred, as we have said, but there is pain at the site, then do not apply bandages; instead, wrap around it with sturdy cloths directly over the bones.
Et quant tu vois aprés I jor ou II enjanrer bowe a la plaie, si oste ceu que tu as mis sus a tout vin, et i met oignement sanant plaies, si com oignement tetrafarmaçon et semblans.	 And when after one or two days you see swelling at the wound, and if you have applied any bone oil that was used previously, then apply healing balm to the wound as an antiseptic like the universal balm ointment.
Et covient que tu deslies lou membre .ij. fois le jor, lou matin et au vespre, tant qu’il soit soudez et sanez.	And it is necessary to loosen the limb twice a day, in the morning and evening, until it is healed and healthy.
Et covient que li membres soit aparilliez en teil maniere que li bowe corre aval legierement.	And it is proper that the limb be braced so that the bow can move gently.
Et se maint jor trespassent, et il ne puet souder mais rent adés bowe, saiches k’il i a petites pieces d’os, por coi il covient que tu quieres la plaie avec tente, et oste toutes ces pieces desevrees que font venir celle dolor.	If more than one day passes and it cannot heal but returns to its bent state, for there are small pieces of bone causing the pain; therefore, you must diligently cover the wound with a bandage and remove all extraneous bones that cause such pain.
Et se fistule vient au leu, ou autre maniere de corruption, si covient que tu le cures, selonc ceu qu’il dist en son chapistre ci devant.	 And if a fistula appears at the site, or another form of decay, it is necessary to treat it accordingly as described in this chapter beforehand.
Et quant li os est brisiez, et apert sus lou membre, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire, et autres semblans des grans membres, si ne le traire mie, car maintes fois en vient li mors, mais le laisse tant qu’il porrisse; par aventure cherra par lui aprés XX jors ou XXX, puis cure la plaie, se tu pues; et se tu ne pues, si la laisse.	 And when the bone is broken and exposed in the limb, as with the hip or shoulder, and other similar injuries to major limbs, do not suture it, for many times this leads to death but leave it until it heals; perhaps it will naturally close after twenty days or thirty. Then treat the wound if you know how; if not, leave it alone.
des brus qui vienent sor la sodure	From bruises which come upon the ulceration
Nous vienent maintes fois aprés la santeit de la briseure, meismement quant c’est pres de la jointure, et laide chose est a veoir li figure dou membre; et par aventure ne puet faire li membres ses ovraiges naturelz.	They often come after the healing of the ulceration, especially when it is near the joint, and an unpleasant thing to see is how the limb appears; and sometimes cannot perform its natural actions.
Pren warde donques se li nous est fres: si li aministre medicines stiptiques, si com aloes, encens, et mirre, et sarcocolle, acaice, et semblans autres, ensi que tu preignes aucune de ces choses, ou toutes ensamble, et les confit avec vin stiptique ou avec abun d’uef ou avec aisil; et les met sus le nout en estoupes, et l’estraint bien, et ne la desliier en mains jors; et puis la desloie, et rencomence une autre, tant que li nodations soit ostee; ou tu estrain sus une piece de plonc bien faite; car li proprietez dou plonc si est qu’il oste toutes les enfleures desus les membres; et se li nodation est ja convertie en durteit ausi com piere, et il est besoing de l’oster, si la cope desus, et fent la superfluiteit apparent; ou tu la reis a aucun raseur, tant qu’ele soit ostee, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee.	Thus beware if the patient is fresh: if you administer stipulative medicines such as aloes, incense, and myrrh, frankincense, and other similar substances, whether taking one of these alone or all together, and mix with astringent wine or an abundance of honey or a syrup; and put on the body in bandages well tightened, and do not loosen them for days. Then release it, and start over with another piece until the swelling is gone; or you may constrain under a well-made plaster as its property that it draws out all inflammation from above the limbs; and if the swelling has already become hard like stone, and needs to be removed, scrape away the excess skin; or take them to a barber who shaves off until they are gone, and heal while still healing.
dou membre qui est foibles aprés la garison	A weak limb after healing
Quant li brisure de l’os est restoree, et demoure aprés li membres foibles et subtilz, si avient por mout de causes: de coi l’une est por ceu qu’il fut liiez trop estroit, et ne fut mie liiez si com il covenoit; ou por ceu qu’il i ot trop de liiens, et ne pooit venir li norrissemens au membre; ou por multitude d’arosement; ou por trop grans movements, ne mie en son houre; ou por ceu qu’il a poc de sanc en son cors, si est foibles.	When the broken bone is restored and remains weak and delicate afterward due to many causes: one being that it was bound too tightly, and not loosened as it should have been; or because there were too many ligatures, preventing circulation in the limb; or due to frequent irritations; or from excessive movements at improper times; or because it has little blood within its body, thus making it weak.
Et li cure si est que tu faices mengier le malaide, et faire le cors tendre, tant que li sans soit multipliiez en lui; et li aministre bain, et li done joie et liesce; puis met poix sus le membre, si que li poix atraie a li grant norrissement, et l’arose sovent d’aigue tede, tant que li norrissement corre au membre; et reviegne a sa figure natureil.	And the treatment is that you should feed the patient well and keep his body relaxed until there are many blood vessels in him again; and give him baths, bringing him joy and cheerfulness; then apply heat to the limb so it draws great nourishment to it, and often remove the cover with cold water, until the nutrition reaches the member; and he returns to his natural shape.
dou membre tort aprés la santeit	Dislocation of a limb after health returns
Quant li membres est tors aprés la restauration, et li os brisiez apert, et li forme dou membre est laide, toutevoie ne pert mie son ovraige natureil: si ne croire mie les folz qui dient c’on doit brisier lou membre tout de noveil, et maint fol mire ont ce fait en nostre terre; et cist ovraiges est blamez, et en vient grans malz, et par aventure li mors; toutevoie, se li nodations et li torture sont fres, si covient k’il soient arosez d’aigue chaude, ou herbes mollifians soient cuites, si com foilles de vismalve, et racines, et mellilote, et semblans choses; et li fai .i. emplaustre mollificatif, si com dyaquilon bien fait, et tu pren le muscillaige de vismalve, et la confit avec graisse de geline ou oile de sisament, et fai emplaustre sus; ou tu pren figues graisses, et les broie avec fien de colon, et semblans medicines que amenuisent le soudement.	When a limb is twisted after restoration and the bones are broken open, and the shape of the affected limb is unsightly, yet it still maintainures its natural workmanship: do not believe the madmen who say that you must break a new member; many foolish people have done so in our land; these practices are blameworthy, and great harm comes from them, sometimes even death. However, if the nerves and twisted bones are fresh, then it is necessary to raise them with hot water, or mollifying herbs cooked as foxglove leaves, roots, meadow-sweet, and similar things; and make a poultice of mallows, like good diaquilon, and take the musk root of vismalwart confit with geese grease or oil of sesame, and apply the poultice. Alternatively, you can use fatty figs ground with flaxseed flour, and other medicines that alleviate swelling.
Et aucune fois est ostee li nodacion por froter continuelment et longement a mains moistes.	 At no time is there bone knitting by constantly and lengthily rubbing with moist hands.
Et soit amenistrez movement au membre chescune houre.	 And so facilitate movement in each limb at any hour.
Et se li tortuositez est enveillie et endurcie, ausi com piere, et besoins est de l’oster au fer, si la covient coper jusc’a l’os, a l’incisoire subtil legierement; et mettre cusenson et estude en la cure.	When the tortuousness is aged and hardened, like a stone, it needs to be removed with iron, if necessary cutting up to the bone, using a delicate saw-like instrument; and place poultices and give careful attention in treatment.
Ci encomence li livres des dislocations	Here begins the book on dislocations
Dislocations est issue d’aucune jointe de son leu, por coi il ne se puet muevre, et est li membres mal figurez, et sent li malaides grant dolor et grant lesion.	Dislocation occurs when a joint moves out of its place, which prevents it from moving, and the limb is misaligned, causing the patient great pain and injury.
Quant dislocation vient a aucun, si le covient maintenant ramener sens targier.	When dislocation occurs on any part, now it must be brought back gently.
Car s’on tarde, si enfle li leus, et par aventure si le remet on a poines au leu; por ceu ne covient mie c’on le mueve a l’oure k’il est enflez: maintes fois fait venir spame et autres dolors; toutevoie, quant ce avenra, si fai sainier lou malaide, puis le laisse, tant que li apostemes chas soit apaisiez; puis arose le membre d’aigue chaude et d’oile, puis le ramoinne legierement, et cure chescun membre si com li cure venra en son leu.	 For if one is late, and the lump has swelled, and if it is painful to return it to its place; therefore, do not move it at the hour when it is inflamed: many times this brings buboes and other pains; however, once this occurs, soothe the patient, then leave them, until the abscess is calmed; then apply warm water and oil to the limb, gently massage each member as treatment appears in its place.
Et j’ai ordenez les chapistres des dislocations des lou chief jusc’a piez.	the s: igne:
des mandibules	Of the lower jawbones
Poc avient que les mandibules soient desaluees andous, et li dislocations d’ambedous est selonc .ij. manieres: ou elles sont un poc ostees de lor leus, et mollifies un poc; ou elles sont desaluees entierement, et pendent vers lou pis, et cort li salive de la bouche qu’il ne la puet tenir, ne ne puet clore sa bouche, et envoloupe sa langue avec la parole.	Sometimes the mandible is dislocated outward, and there are two ways of dislocation: either it's slightly off from its place and swolps a bit; or it is entirely dislocated, hanging toward the cheek, causing saliva to not be held in the mouth nor able to close the mouth, enveloping the tongue during speech.
Quant li dislocations est petite, si revient par li em plusors disposicions.	When the dislocation is slight, it may return through various positions.
Et s’elle est entiere et acomplie, si covient que tu la ramoinne hastanment, et ne targier mie; et en tel maniere que li ministres teigne le chief dou malaide, et boute li mires som pochet de l’une de ses mains en la racine de la dislocation de la mandibule dedens la bouche, se li dislocations est de II pars; et li autre doi des mains soient defuer, por mettre igal; et comande au malaide qu’il les amollisse, ses mandibules, et les mueve de toutes pars.	 And if it is complete and done, then hasten to massage it gently without squeezing; in such a manner that the medicinal substance colors the head of the patient, and pour a few drops from one hand into the root of the dislocation of the jawbone inside the mouth, wherein the dislocation is divided into two parts; and let the other hand be free to balance it. Then command the patient to soften his mandibles, and move them in all directions.
Et li mires la mete igal, tant qu’elle reveigne en son leu.	, et que rist of his a lassue les peux sores: ici au de pain, ou jucle dis locations they mandres so the cemai; deter the plaster and pain ee, that the patient, but for it beand li brize. Andre, par ces ointenz saignent tis, duces of l’esquiter les, çui la de la m si vaille jue le disin their toile s;
Et se li ramener est griés, meismement se ce sont les .ij. mandibules ensamble, si les arose d’aigue chaude et d’oile, tant que les ramoinnes legierement; ne ne targier mie dou ramener, si com nos avons dit.	If it is difficult to reset, especially if they are the two lower jaws together, use hot water and oil until gently relocated; do not wrench while doing so, as we have said.
Et quant elles sont ramenees igalment, et li bouche dou malaide clot bien sens mollifiier, si met sus drapelz moilliez en cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire, puis le lie legierement de molz liiens; et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ses chiés soit estans entre II cussins, si qu’il ne lou mueve ne a destre ne a senestre, ne ne s’efforce mie de maixier, mais preigne legiere viande, tant que les dolors soient ostees, et soient noees les mandibules; et puis menjuce ce qu’il vuet legierement, et ne se travaille mie d’ovrir la bouche au mengier et au boivre, tant que li mandibule soit bien noee et sanee.	 When they are equally returned, the patient's mouth closes well and feels softened; then place a cloth moistened with an ointment made of rose oil and wax, after which lightly bind it with soft ties; let the patient sleep on their back, with their head between two pillows so that they do not move to either side or strain themselves. Encourage them to eat easy meat until the pains are gone, and the jaws have been fully bathed and cleansed; then allow what they wish for a light meal without forcing them to open their mouth while eating or drinking, as long as the mandibles remain well-soaked and healthy.
Et se les .ij. mandibules ne pueent estre remises a point a une houre, et ne sont mie converties a lor leus, si en vient fievres et sode acostumees, et par aventure solution de ventre, et par aventure vomist cole pure.	Et si les deux mâchoires ne peuvent être remises à leur place en une heure, ni repositionnées correctement, alors on peut avoir des fièvres habituelles, diarrhée ou nausée avec vomissements purulents occasionnellement.
Et quant tu verras ceu, adonc saiches que c’est perdicions; et maintes fois muert cil cui il avient, en .viiij. jors.	Et quand vous observez cela, alors vous savez qu'il s'agit d'une perte ; de nombreuses fois ceux qui souffrent meurent au cours des sept jours suivants.
de la forcelle	Of the joint's forcefulness
Li forcele ne puet desaluer dou costeit dedens la continuation de li et dou pis, et est desaluee aucune fois au defuer, et bien le sent on.	The strength cannot be dislocated within the ribcage and lower region, and is never dislocated easily, causing much pain to those who experience it.
Et li restauration si est que li malaides gise sovin sor son dos, et estende ses bras; et puis presse le leu forment a ta palme, et elle revenra; puis met sus l’emplaustre et lou bendeil, et l’estraint; et li chiez qui est devers lou coute ne puet desaluer; se poc non, et se il desalue aucune fois, si le ramoinne a son leu, si com nos avons dit; puis met sus l’emplaustre et le bendeil, et l’estraint, et coumande au malaide qu’il se repose tant qu’il soit sanez; et ensi meisme est ramenez li chiés de l’espale, quant il est desevrez de son leu.	 The restoration method is that the patient lies on their back and extends their arms; then firmly press the joint with your palm, and it will return; then apply heat to the area and a poultice, and immobilize; and the leg which is towards the couch cannot dislocate again; if not possible, or if it does so at any time, reset it to its place as we have said; then apply heat to the area and a poultice, and immobilize, and instruct the patient to rest until they are well; similarly, this method is used for bringing back the shoulder blade when dislocated from its position.
de la dislocation de l’espaule	Of shoulder dislocation
Saiches que li espaule n’est desaluee fuer que selonc III manieres: de coi l’une est qu’ele desalue a la partie de l’assele au desoz; et li seconde est a la partie dou pis; et par aventure desalue a la partie desus, et ceu avient poc; et ne desalue mie derrier por l’espaule, et ne desalue mie dedens por les ners; et plusors fois desalue desoz vers l’assele, meismement a ces qui ont poc de char, car a ces saut ele fuer hastanment; a ces qui ont assez char, saut ele a poines, et rentre a poines.	 We say that the shoulder is dislocated in three ways: one way where it dislocates from the lower part of the arm; and another at the upper part of the arm; and occasionally above, which happens rarely; and does not dislocate backwards nor internally near the nerves; and often dislocates towards the forearm, especially in those with little flesh, because to these it moves quickly; and for those with enough flesh, it moves easily but returns just as quickly.
Et par aventure avient a aucuns homes percussion ou casseure, et enfle li espaule d’un aposteme chaut, et cuide qu’elle est desaluee par ceu.	And sometimes it happens to certain men with a blow or fracture, and the shoulder swells from a hot abscess, and they think that it is dislocated due to this.
Il covient donques que tu l’esprueves, tant que tu en soies certains; et adonques encomence la cure.	It therefore requires you to test it until certainty is achieved; then begin the treatment.
Et est conue li dislocations quant il est aval vers l’assele, et met difference entre l’espaule malade et la saine, et tu troveras entre lor diversiteit manifeste; et troveras au chief de l’espaule une fosse, et desoz l’assele au tochier le chief de l’espaule, ausi com se ce soit uns oes; et ne puet li malaides ramener sa main a son neis, ne movoir de nulz movemens; et ausi, s’elle est desaluee en haut, si n’est mie occultee, car tu le trueves manifestement au tochier; et ceste maniere de dislocation n’est mie fors a ramener, quant elle est novele, ou se li enfes est malaides.	 And it is known that with dislocation when it moves towards the axle, and there is a difference between the affected shoulder and the healthy one, and you will find their diversity obvious; and you will find at the top of the shoulder a hollow, and below the shoulder where the top of the shoulder meets, just as if it were some ears; and the patient cannot bring his hand to its place, nor move in any way; similarly, if it is dislocated upward, it is not hidden, for you can clearly find it at the axle; and this kind of dislocation is not only to be realigned when it is new or if the child feels unwell.
Et li maniere est que li ministres lieve la main dou malaide en haut, puis met tes peuchas desoz l’assele, et lieve la jointure a force en haut au leu; et li ministres lieve la main, et l’estende en haut, pues le mette desoz; si venra hastanment.	And the manner is that the minister lifts the patient's hand upward, then removes the shoulder blade and lifts the joint forcefully back to its place; the minister lifts the hand again and extends it upwards, placing it beneath; this will be done swiftly.
Et s’elle ne vient si com nos avons dit em mains jors aprés, si covient ke li malaides soit baigniez en aigue chaude; et li amenistre arosement mollifiant et assouajant, si com decoction de altee et de fenugrec et de mellilote en aigue, et soit amenistree; puis soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos, et mette on desoz l’assele un sto de lainne igal, ne trop mol ne trop dur, puis mette li mires son talon sus le sto, et lieve le chief de l’espaule vertuousement, et traie la main dou malaide; et uns autres ministres teigne lou chief dou malaide, si qu’il ne se mueve aval; celle espaule revient tout maintenant, et se tu vues si le ramoinne selonc ceste maniere: et est que tu faices estre present I home qui soit plus grans que li malaides; et soit drois devers lou costeit, et boute s’espaule desoz l’assele dou malaide, et lieve l’assele en haut, si que li malaides pende en l’ar; et uns autres ministres traie la main dou malaide aval devers lou ventre.	 And if it does not come as we have said within a few days, then the child should be bathed in warm water; and soothe them with moistening and calming substances, such as an infusion of elderflower and fenugreek and milletwort in water, and apply it; then place the child on his back, and under the shoulder put a strap equal, neither too soft nor too hard, then place the fingers of the hand below the malaid's heel, and lift the top of the shoulder gently, and move the limb upwards with your hand; another minister treats the head of the malaide so that it does not move forward; this shoulder returns immediately now, and if you see the joint according to this method: and make sure a man who is taller than the malaid is present; and stand beside him, and place the shoulder below the malaides back, and lift the shoulder upwards, so that the child hangs in the air; another minister moves the hand of the meblade towards their belly.
Et se li malaides est trop legiers, si pent avec lui aucune chose pesant, et li dislocation revient maintenant.	 And if the patient is too lightweight, reinforce them with something heavy so that the dislocation does not return now.
Et le ramoinne on ausi en autre maniere: et est c’on fiche I lonc tison en terre, dont li chiés soit ausi reons com I pistal, et ne soit ne trop gros ne trop graile; puis soit mis desoz lou malaide, mais k’il ait drapelz souef sus, et li malaides soit estans dou lonc dou fust; puis soit estendue sa main aval d’autre part forment, et li jointure revenra en son leu hastanment; et s’elle ne vuet revenir por toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si fai ceste cure: pren I tison de II bras de grant et IIII dois de large, qui ait le chief reont por mues entrer em parfont desoz l’assele, selonc ceste forme:	 And the joint can be treated in another way: it is that one makes a long stick and buries it into the ground so that its top level with the patient's shoulder blade, neither too thick nor too narrow; then place it behind the patient, ensuring they have sufficient padding above, while the patient lies on their long back firmly; then stretch out their hand to the opposite side properly; and the joint will return to its place quickly. And if it does not return for all these reasons we mentioned, do this treatment: take a stick of two arm's length and four thumbs wide, which has one end pointed so that it can enter straight back under the shoulder according to this shape:
puis lie sus le chief dou fust drapelz souez, que li fust ne blece lou malaide, puis le met desoz l’assele dou malaide; et estende som bras sus le fust dou lonc, et lie l’ajutoire sus le fust, et lou bras au chief de la main, puis met le bras sus .i. eschillon d’une eschiele dou large, et soit estendue li mains aval, et soit laissiez li cors pendans d’autre part: li jointure reva ens maintenant.	Then wrap the head with soft cloths so they do not prick the patient, then place it under the neck of the sick person; extend your arms over the length of a staff, and secure the shoulder to the staff, with the arm at the top of the hand, then put the arm above an arch of a wide stretcher, let the hands hang downward, and leave the body hanging on the other side: the joints will be now secured.
Et quant elle est ens, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient que tu mettes desoz l’assele une spere de laine igal, puis met l’emplaustre aparilliet de poudre dou molin, avec encens et aubun d’uef, sus toute l’espaule et entor, puis l’estrain desoz l’assele avenanment, et torne le liien sus l’emplaustre, et embraice la main a son col, et soit li mains demorans ensi.	And when it is done in any way at all, if you must place under the neck of a spindle threaded with wool equally, then apply the poultice fitted with powder from grinding, with incense and egg yolk around the entire shoulder and near it, then strain off liquid from the poult groove.
Et covient qu’il menjuce poc, tant que li membres soit confortez, car il sanera plus tost; et puis menjuce plus aprés .v. jors ou .vij., et le mueve; et s’il est fermeis et il n’est mollifiez, si est sanez.	It is necessary that it heal as soon as the members are strengthened so it will be more days or less than five and then move; and if it is firm and let them loose, if not stiffen.
Et se li jointure est fuer de leu por moistor que i est venue, ou por autre cause, si covient que tu i aministres cauteres a III pertus, si com il est mis devant ou chapistre des cauteres.	 And if the joint is forced out by moisture or another reason, it must be treated with three small cauterizations as described in the chapter on cauteries.
Et se tu fais tout ceu, et il deslie aprés .vij. jors, et li jointure ne se tient, et ne puet lever som bras amont, adonc saiches que li nerf au chief de l’espaule sont copeit ou estendut ou amollis; et saiches que li jointure n’iert jamais fichie en son leu.	And if you do all this, and it dislocates again after six or seven days, and the joint does not hold and cannot lift either arm forward, then know that the nerve at the top of the shoulder is compressed or stretched out or weakened; and know that the joint will never be fixed in its place.
Li dislocation qui est devers lou pis, et les mameles, ou derrier, si est faite par impulsion, et estendement de mains, et i aministre on autre lieure; et cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	The dislocation towards the back and buttocks is caused by a blow, and extension of the arms, and you must administer other remedies; treat until it heals.
Et se aprés la sanation vient grietez au membre, et tardemens em movement, si use li malaides bain maintes fois, tant que celle grietez soit alegie, et reviegne a sa premiere nature.	And if after healing comes stiffness to the limb and sluggish movements, many times it is used on the patient until the stiffness eases and returns to its original state.
de la dislocation dou coute	Of dislocation of the joints in the shoulder blade.
Saiches que li jointure dou coute est desaluee a poinnes, et a poinnes revient; et s’est desaluee de toutes pars, et meismement devant et derrier, et li dislocations n’est mie reponue, car on la voit bien et sent bien; et desalue selonc chescune figure.	He says that the joint of the shoulder blade is displaced to points, and returns to points; and it has been displawed from all parts, especially in front and back, and dislocation is not properly reduced because one can see it well and feel it well; and displaced according to each figure.
Et quant tu joins le coute malaide avec lou sain, si le pues veoir apertement.	 And when you join the bad joint with its bone, if you can see it clearly.
Car li jointure est chevee, et ne puet ploier lou bras, ne touchier son espaule a tout.	 For the joint is raised, and cannot bend the arm or touch its shoulder at all.
Et covient que tu le ramoinnes ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne, car se apostemes chaus i venoit, si seroit grief li ramener; et par aventure ne puet estre ramenez dou tout en tout, meismement quant ele est au derrier; si vaut pis que les autres dislocations, et est de plus grant dolor, et par aventure i vient li mors.	And it must be reset as soon as abscesses arise therein, for if they come to pass, the repositioning would be difficult; and sometimes not all of it can be reset at once, especially when it is in the back; such dislocations are worse than others, causing greater pain, and possibly leading to death.
Et li restauration si est, quant elle est telz c’on la puet ramener, que tu li estendes sa main a tes .ij. mains; et ses bras soit espandus, et les mains dou mire selonc le coute entor, desor et desoz, et boute la jointure a ses peuchas ensamble, ou a la racine de sa palme, tant qu’ele reviegne a son leu.	And the restoration is when it can be reset, extend its hand to your two hands; and arms are spread apart, and hands according to the bone around, above and below, place the joint back together or at the root of its palm, until it returns to its place.
Et se li dislocations est au devant, si revient quant il double sa main a sa main, et fier de la racine de la palme lou coute qui est desaluez.	And if the dislocation is at the front, when it doubles its hand to its own hand, and the root of the palm's hinge that is dislocated.
Et s’il ne vuet revenir au leu, si aministre fort extension; et est que dui ministre estendent le bras, et le teignent dui ministre, si qu’il ne se mueve a l’estension; puis torne le bras de chescune part, puis que tu as envoloupeit un drapeil double lonc et large; et quant li mires a jointe la jointure a sa main, si l’oigne d’aucun oile por amolir la jointure, puis boute la jointure forment, tant qu’ele reviegne; et quant elle est au leu, si met sus emplaustre sec avec aubun d’uef, et l’estrain forment, et pent le bras au col dou malaide, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le deslie.	 And if it does not return to place, administer strong extension; and two ministers extend the arm, and tie with their ropes, so that it does not move during extension; then turn the arm in each direction, after enveloping a double wide and long cloth; and when the joint is connected to its bone again, anoint it with any oil to soften the joint, then press the joint firmly until it regains position; and once it is back in place, apply dry oatmeal with egg whites, strain firmly, and immobilize the arm at the painful side for several days.
Et se li jointure est ferme en son leu, si deslie lou liien, et le laisse; et se tu vois que li jointure n’estrigne bien, si rencomence l’emplaustre et lou lien, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit fermement mis; puis le deslie.	If the joint is firmly in place, then release it and leave it; and if you see that the joint does not hold well, reapply the paste and bandage again, and leave it for several days until it is securely set; then release it.
Et se il sent grieteit aprés le ramenement de la jointe, et elle se muet, si le baigne et frote bellement, et presse tant qu’il soit assouagiez; ou tu met sus la jointure une naige de mouton grasse, puis la laisse I jor et une nuit, puis l’oste, et lou fai entrer ou bain; et quant il sue, se li frote la jointure tempreement, puis remet la naige sus, et puis entre ou bain; et ensi fai II fois ou III, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vues, si met sus fien de vaiche moiste chaufeit avec burre, et l’estrain sus; si revenra a sa disposition.	 And if after resetting the joint it feels instability and moves, then bathe and rub well, and press until soothed; or put on the joint a piece of fatty mutton wool, then leave for a day and night, then bandage, and let them take a bath; and when they sweat, rub the joint tenderly, then replace the mutton wool, and then bathe; thus do it twice or three times until healed; if you see this, put on moist warm barley ashes with butter, and bind over; it will return to its position.
li dislocation de la main	Hand dislocation
Li jointure de la main desalue, et li revenue est legiere, plus que les autres jointures Toutevoie, il la covient ramener au leu hastanment, en l’oure meisme qu’ele est desaluee, ainsois que li leus soit enflez, ou qu’il i viegne aposteme chaut.	The dislocation of the hand is slight, and its return is easy compared to other joints Therefore, it must be promptly returned to its place at once when dislocated, so that it may swell or develop an abscess as soon as possible.
Et li ramenemens si est que tu mettes la main malaide sus une tauble, et estende li ministres la main, et li mires la mette igal, ensi que il mette sa paume sus l’aparance de la jointure, et la boute tant qu’elle reviegne Toutevoie, il covient que vos regardez s’il est bien a leu; adonc mette li malaides lou dos de sa main sus une tauble a l’estension et au ramenement.	 The readjustments are that you place the patient's hand on a table, extend the fingers, and align them so they can put their palm over the joint area, pressing until it is correctly aligned; then ensure it has been properly reset before having them hold onto a straightened arm to maintain the adjustment.
Et se li dislocations est au dos de la main, si mette li malaides son dos de sa main sus la tauble, et li mires mette sa main sus cele apparance de la jointure.	 And if the dislocation is in the back of the hand, make the patient place their hand's back on a table, and let the physician place his hand under that appearance of the joint.
S’elle revient maintenant, c’est bien Se ce non, si l’estrain d’emplaustres apaisans apostemes chaus, et lou laisse ensi sens rencomencier.	 If it returns now, then well; if not, apply the strain of soothing balms and ointments for abscesses, and let them be thus re-examined again.
Et s’il ne le puet soffrir, et tu ne la pues mettre au leu aprés aucuns jors, si demore li jointure torte; et ne nuist niant au malaide fuer que tant que li mains est amoillie, et ne puet estraindre aucune chose a tout: adonc saiches que li nerf sont copez, ou li artere; si n’i a autre engien fuer que d’estraindre par cautere delez le cas, et par aventure n’i vaut autre chose.	 And if it cannot be endured by him and you cannot place it back in its place after several days, the joint remains twisted; and neither this nor that can move anything for the patient until his hand becomes softened, and he is unable to grasp anything: then understand that a nerve or an artery has been cut off, or there is no other remedy than to pull it back with a caustic near the joint, and perhaps nothing else works.
Et quant li mains est au leu, si met sus l’emplaustre que nos avons dit, puis l’estrain et le laisse .v. jors, puis le deslie et laisse ensi.	but;
Et s’il ne la puet bien movoir, et il i a aucune grieteit, si la moille d’aigue chaude, et le frote tant qu’il soit sanez.	If it cannot be moved properly, and there is no sharpness, then warm water of milk, and rub until it becomes smooth.
de la dislocation des dois de la main	Of the dislocation of hand bones
Aucune fois sont desaluez li doi de la main a chescune part, aucune fois au dos de la palme ou au ventre; adonques estent le doi, et boute la dislocation a tes pouchés tant qu’il reviegne, puis sostien lou chief dou doi, et le pent vers la partie ou il est desjoins; et le laisse II jors, et puis le met igal celui jor; et de nut le lie, si com nos avons dit, et lou deslie de jor, et lou fai movoir, et le relie la nut; et fai ce sovent, tant qu’il soit estroit, et tout ausi fai, se il est desaluez au ventre de la main, et fai si com tu as fait ci devant, tant qu’il soit sanez; et tout ausi fai, quant il est desaluez d’autre part.	 On no occasion are the two bones of the hand dislocated to either side, nor at the back of the palm or stomach; then they move as if locked in place and the dislocation remains within your grasp until it returns, then support the head of the joint, and turn towards the part where it is disjointed; leave them for two days, and then make them even on that day; and no more do you bind, as we have said, and the daily unbinding, and causing movement, and re-binding; and perform this often, until they are straightened, and just as before, if dislocated at the stomach of the hand, continue to do so until it is aligned properly; and similarly treat when dislocated from another part.
dou desaluement de l’eschinee dou dos	Of the displacement of the spine of the back
Quant l’eschinee dou dos ou dou col est desaluee, ou il en i a plusors desaluees, si n’i a point de cure, car li mors haste le malaide.	When the spine of the back or neck is dislocated, and there are several dislocations, there is no remedy, for it hastens death to the patient.
Et li signes si est que li egestions saut fuer sens volunteit, ne ne la puet tenir, et maintes fois sont mollifiez aucun membre, ou les II cuixes ou li dui bras ou I Et maintes fois se muet li eschinee a IIII pars; celle qui se muet au derrier si est apelee «gilbositez»: li cure si est que tu rewarde se li gilbositez est venue d’enfance: si n’i ait point de cure ne de sanation dou tot.	 The signs are that the excretions fall without willingness, cannot be held, and many times limbs are weakened, either both thighs or one arm or leg; often the spine dislocates in two parts; those whose vertebrae dislocate at the back are called "hollowed out": treatment is to return them where they were from childhood, if there has been no cure or healing entirely.
Et celle que vient de cheoir ou de percussions ou de semblans choses, dirent li ancien manieres de cures par grans paroles, ou il n’a mie en toutes grant profit; mais je l’ai abregiet selonc mon entention, et ai formez estrumens en diverses manieres.	 And those that arise from falling or striking or other matters are treated by old methods with many words, which brings no great benefit; but I have abbreviated them according to my intention and formed remedies in various ways.
Je dis que en la gilbositeit que vient au pis devant, nen a engien ne santeit; et ausi cele que vient droitement en II costez, et ne puet on curer fuers que celi proprement qui vient au dos, si com je dis; et est que li malaides soit estendus sus sa faice en I leu igal, et ait de l’estrain desoz lui, qu’il ne se blece; puis fiche I tison au chief en terre forment, et I autre as piez, et lie un liien pardesoz les asseles dou malaide, et I autre as hainches, et as genous, et as chevilles; et dui ministre saichent les liiens, li uns au chief et li autres as piez, parmi les II tisons; et soient bien fermez, li tison si com nos avons dit, et li mires mette ses paumes sus l’espinee forment, tant qu’ele reviegne.	 In the swelling that occurs at the front of the thigh, there is neither remedy nor health; similarly with those that come straight to both sides, and they cannot be cured unless by what properly comes on the back, as I say; and it must be that the patient lies extended on his face in equal places, and should have strain off from him, so he does not move. Then stick a tine at the head flatly into the earth, and another at the foot, and tie with cord around the joints of the patient's malady, and another around the calves, and knees, and ankles; and two ministers know the cords, one on the head and the other on the feet, among the twins. And they are well fastened as we have said, and the master sets his palms firmly along the spine properly, until it straightens out.
Et s’elle ne revient par ceste cure, si pren une tauble de III bras de lonc, et chevé desoz la paroit, et li malaides soit en costé, et boute le chief de la tauble desoz la paroit, puis met le mileu de la tauble sus l’espinee; et mette li mires ses piez sus l’autre chief de la tauble, et presse bien, tant qu’il reviegne au leu; et se tu vues, si le fai au tornet qui torne a la main.	 If it does not return through this method, take a stick three arms' length long, and lift from the surface, and let the patient lie on their side, then place the head of the stick under the surface, next put the middle of the stick over the spine; then set the ends of the stick against the other end of the head, and press firmly until it returns to its place; and if you see this, turn the torment that turns towards the hand.
Et est que tu fiches II tisons au chief dou malaide d’un bras de grant, et devers les piez II autres, et ait entre chescun tison, desoure et desoz, une paume d’espaice de lonc; et ait en chescun tison I pertus, ou li tornet corre, et soient li tison fermement en terre, si qu’il ne se muevent; et entre chescuns II tisons ait I tison tornant, sor coi li liien tornent, et ait en II tornans II petis tisons d’une paume de lonc, por torner le tornet; et puis lie lou lien qui est parmi les asseles au tornet devers le chief, et l’autre liien devers les piez a l’autre tornet, et chescuns des ministres torne son tornet a tout le liien, et li maistres mette l’espinee igal si com nos avons dit.	 And you shall insert two ties at the head of the patient's arm lengthwise, and towards the other ends, with space equivalent to an arm's width between each tie on both sides; and in each tie, one loop or turn is correct, and they are firmly placed so that they do not move. Between each pair of ties, there should be a turning tie at which the ligaments turn, and two small ties of an arm'e length to rotate the torment; then the master places the ligament between the joints towards one end of the torment as we have described, and the other ligament towards the ends on the opposite side, and each assistant turns their respective torment around all its ligaments.
Et quant elle est igalz, si met sus emplaustre desiccatif avec abun d’uef, et puis les estoupes, et puis l’estele d’une tablete de III dois de lonc, que porpreigne lou leu de la gilbositeit et la partie de l’espondile sainne, puis le lie d’un liien, si com nos avons dit, et use li malaides de norrissement subtil, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’aucune chose vient en la fin de la santez, si covient aministrer medicines amollissans et asouajans, avec l’estele que nos avons dit ci devant; et aucune fois i aministre on une piece de plonc, et aucune fois vient li apparance en la derriere spondile dou dos, et cuide on que ce soit dislocations; et c’est li os qui apert, por coi on n’i doit mie avoir presumption: par aventure feroit venir la mort.	 When they are equalized, place the dried styptic with an abundance of wax, then the staples, and then the splint of a tablet III fingers long to support the site of the bone breakage and the healthy part of the spine, then bandage it with a ligature as we have said, and instruct the patient in subtle nourishment until they are well; and if anything arises at the end of their healing, administer medicines that soften and soothe, with the splint as mentioned before; and never apply a piece of lead, nor does the appearance come to the rear spine vertebrae, assuming it is dislocation; these are fractured bones for which there should be no presumption: perhaps it would cause their death.
des dislocations de la hainche	for hip joint dislocations
Saiches que as jointures de la hainche et as jointures de l’espaule ne vient fuers que dislocacions soulement, ne n’i vient mie si com as autres jointures; et li jointure de la hainche est desaluee selonc .iiij. parties: dedens et defuer ,et devant et derrier; et plus dedens c’aillors, et poc desalue devant et derrier.	Joints of the thigh and shoulder joints do not experience sprains but only dislocations, unlike other joints; the thigh joint is dislocated in four parts: internally and externally, front and back, more internally than externally, and slightly less so at the front and back.
Et li conoissance de sa dislocations dedens si est que quant on joint la jambe malaide avec la sainne, si est plus longe, et apert plus li malaides genous que li sains, et ne puet li malaides doubler son genoil au feu; et est li leus qui est delez enflez d’aposteme chaut, por ceu que li chiés de la cuixe vient lai.	 And the knowledge of its dislocation is such that when you join the affected leg with the healthy one, it becomes longer and opens up more bursae on the sick side than the healthy, so the patient cannot fold his foot over fire; and there are swollen lumps near an abscess due to the hip's head coming close.
Et li signe de celui cui il vient au defuer, si est que cist accident sont contraire a ces devant.	And the sign of those it comes upon by chance, is such that this accident is contrary to these before.
Et li signes de celui cui avient au devant, si est qu’il estent bien sa jambe selonc l’acomplissement; toutevoie, ne double mie le genoil sens dolor, et s’on le vuet faire aler, si ne puet avant, et retient son urine, et enfle li angre, et quant il vait, si passe sus le talon.	And the signs of those it happens upon, are such that they walk well with their legs in accordance; however, do not double over in pain at the groin, and if one wishes them to walk, they cannot beforehand, retains urine, and swells the ankle, and when walking, passes above the heel.
Et li signes de celui cui il avient derrier, si est qu’il ne puet espandre son genoil, ne doubler, et est celle jambe plus torte de l’autre, et li angre est mollifié, et est li chiés de la cuixe au leu desoz les costes.	And s and thent; That dose ce que the test.
Li ramenemens de ceste semblance de dislocation si est que tu rewarde se li dislocations est anciainne, et elle demore selonc sa disposition, si n’i a nule cure; et n’i covient mie qu’il ait presumption.	The resetting of this type of dislocation is such that you may reposition it before the dislocation occurs, and it remains according to its nature, there is no need for treatment; and it does not require any assumption.
Et en celi dont li dislocation est fresche, et c’est des .iiij. manieres de dislocation, si te haste que tu tornes la jointe, et l’esten dedens et defuer, et la muef a destre et senestre; par aventure si revenra, et n’a mestier d’autre cure.	And in those cases where the dislocation is fresh and there are four ways of dislocating it, quickly return to the joint, push it back and forward, and move it to the right and left; perhaps it will return by itself, and requires no other treatment.
Et s’il ne revient en ceste maniere, si covient que tu apareilles I ministre fort, et esten la jambe fort a II mains, ou a I liien que soit liiez sus lou genoil; et uns autres ministres estende sa main desus en teil maniere qu’il boute ses mains desoz ses asseles, puis l’estrigne d’un souef liien sus la cuixe; et uns autres tigne lou chief dou liien; et estendent amont et aval tuit a une fois, tant que li malaide soit levez de terre a une fois, et demoure pendans.	 And if it does not return this way, then prepare a strong minister and secure the leg firmly in two bands or with a band that is wrapped above the ankle; another method extends its hand over it like placing hands under its heels, then grips it tightly with a thin band below the hip; others pull on the ligament. Extend all up and down once, until the patient is raised off the ground once, and remains hanging.
Ceste maniere d’estension si est commune as .iiij. semblances, et se li dislocation est revenue, si com nos avons dit, c’est bien.	This method of extension is common in four similar cases; if the dislocation has returned, as we have said, it is good.
Se ceu non, si covient mettre cure a sa semblance Quant li dislocations est au pardedens, si covient que tu sovines le malaide sus son costeit sain, puis met le liien sus la racine de la cuixe, et le leu qui est desoz l’angre, puis estent le liien en haut devers l’angre, et devers la forcele; puis preigne uns autres ministres ses bras, et embraice le gros leu de la cuixe malaide, et l’estende au defuer forment: si revenra a son leu maintenant; et ceste maniere de dislocation est plus legiere des autres.	 If that is not the case, then attention must be given to its appearance when the dislocation occurs in the jawbone; it is necessary to support the patient on their chest with soundness, then place a ligature at the base of the thigh, and extend the ligature towards the groin, and upwards towards the abdomen; other assistants should hold its arms, and wrap the large area of the affected thigh, extending it forward properly: this will return to its place now; this method of dislocation is easier compared to others.
Et se tu ne la pues serrer en ceste maniere que nos avons dit, si covient que tu lies les II piés dou malaide ensamble d’un fort liien souef sus les II talons, et sus les II genous, et soit li jambe malaide estendue II dois plus que li autres; puis soit pendus sus le chief d’un fust, et soit en sus de terre II bras de lonc; puis comande a I ministre qu’il embraice le chief de la cuixe, et soit uns autres ministres pendans avec le malaide, qui embraice forment la cuixe, car li jointure revient maintenant hastanment.	 And if you cannot hold it in this way as we have described, then with a strong supple ligature bind both feet of the affected person together at the heels and knees, and keep the affected leg extended two fingers more than the other; then hang them from the head of a beam, and their arms long off the ground; then instruct an assistant to embrace the thigh's head, and have others hanging with the affected individual who will firmly embrace the thigh, as the joints return quickly now.
Et quant li dislocations est au defuer, si gise li malaides, si com nos avons dit en celui qui a gilbositeit, et estraigne I liien sus la jambe malaide proprement, et sus le peis ausi; puis met II tisons, I au chief et I autre as piez, puis fiche I tison entre les cuixes au malaide emmi la forme; et ait plantei de drapelz moistes entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide, puis estende chescuns ministre devers lui, et li mires mette igal a sa main la dislocation.	 And when the dislocation is underneath, place the tiles so that they are correctly positioned on the affected leg and foot; then insert two wicks at the head and another between the toes; afterward, moisten the bandages around it without shifting the limb, then stretch them out toward him. The patient's counterpart places his hand in alignment with the dislocation.
S’elle revient, c’est boin.	 If it returns, that is well-made (or 'good'). This refers to the successful repositioning of a dislocated
Se ce non, met sus .ie. table, et le presse ensi com nos avons dit en la gilbositeit, et gise li malaides sus le sain costeit.	 If not, place him on a board and press as we have described for the dislocation of the hip joint; position the patient's body correctly over it.
Et quant li dislocations est devant, si covient estendre la jambe malaide hastanment, et selonc ce que j’ai dit; et mette li mires sa paine d’estre sus l’angre malaide, puis presse a l’autre main, et l’estent aval devers lou genoil.	And when the dislocation is in front, it must extend the injured leg quickly, and according to what I have said; then place the physician's hand on the painful side, then press with the other hand, and stretch downwards towards the groin.
Et se li dislocations est au defuer, si ne covient pas estendre le malaide aval, ne lever sus la terre, ains covient qu’il soit ausi com se li hainche estoit desaluee au defuer, si com nos avons dit dou couchement sus les II hainches; et soit sus sa faice, et li lien estendut si com nos avons dit ci devant, et doit om presser sus la jointure a la table; et sera a point quant li malaides estendra ses jambes, et elles seront igalz; adonques ajoste les cuixes, et met l’emplaustre, et l’estrain d’un bendeil, si que li hainche ne se mueve; et se repose III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie, et met l’emplaustre sus; et se tu vois qu’elles soient igalz, si l’estrain, si com devant, et le laisse III jors; puis le deslie, et lou fai aler belement, tant que li membres soit confortez.	 If the dislocation is in the back, it does not require extending the patient's legs or lifting from the ground, but they should remain as if the hip was dislocated backwards during sleep on both hips; then placed against their face, and the limb extended as previously described, pressing must be applied to the joint at the table; when the patient extends his legs, and they will be even; thus position the buttocks, place the cast, and wrap with a bandage so that the hip does not move; then rest for three days or four, afterwards release, and apply the cast again; if you see them are even, as before, leave it on for three more days.
de la dislocation dou genoil	De la dislocation du genou
Li genous est desaluez selonc .iij. manieres: c’est a savoir, dedens et defuer, et derrier; et ne desalue point devant.	I nternal and external displacement occurs in three ways: that is to say, within and outward, and behind; it does not displace forward.
Et li signes si est que tu comande au malaide qu’il plie sa jambe a sa cuixe, et s’ele ne s’aert a sa cuixe, saiches qu’il est desaluez; et li restauration de toutes si est que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et estende sa jambe s’il puet, et li met ton dos sus sa faice, et met son piet sus tes piez; puis pren son genoil a tes paumes, et retrai entre tes dois, puis plie les II costez dou genoil forment; et uns autres ministres estende son piet, tant que li genous reviegne a son leu, et li signes est qu’il aert bien sa jambe a sa cuixe legierement; et met l’emplastre sus, et fai aerdre la jambe a la cuixe, et les loie ensamble fort III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie; et ne se travaille mie li malaides d’aler, tant que li membres soit confortez.	 The signs are that you command the patient to bend his leg at the thigh, and if it doesn't reach the thigh, know that it is dislocated; and in its restoration, have the patient sit upright, extend the limb as much as possible, place your back against their face, and put your foot under yours. Then take hold of his ankle with your hands, then slip between your fingers, then bend both shins formidably; other assistants extend the foot, until the knee joint returns to its place, and the sign is that it lightly touches the thigh; apply the plaster on top, make the leg fit snugly against the thigh for 3-4 days or more, then release it; and do not let the patient move about while ensuring comfort.
Et se li membres n’est a point, si aministre estendement fort, si com nos avons dit en la cure de la hainche, tant qu’il soit sanez	 And if the limb is not functioning well, it should be strengthened greatly, as we have said in the treatment of the knee, until it becomes healthy.
de la dislocation dou talon	Regarding ankle dislocation
Li talons est aucune fois esmeus, et aucune fois desaluez plenement, et dedens et defuer.	The heel is at no time fully bent, nor fully straightened completely, but sometimes forward and backward.
Et li signes si est que li cheville est enflee, et tent avant a la partie ou elle est desaluee: li ramenemens si est legier, et le doit on estendre legierement a ses mains quant il est esmeus soulement.	 And the signs are such that the ankle is dislocated, and before reaching the part where it has been displaced: the reductions should be gentle, and one must gently extend with their hands once barely touched.
Et quant il est desaluez dou tot, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et le tigne I ministres fors par la jambe, desus la cheville; puis trai le piet a toi a ta main destre, et puis a la senestre II fois, puis l’estent en haut, et boute bellement lou piet en haut; et fai ce II fois, si com nos avons dit, em boutant et en traiant lou piet; s’elle revient, c’est bien; se ce non, si rencomence l’ovraige, car il revient; et s’il ne puet revenir ensi, si fai gesir lou malaide sor son dos sus terre, et fiche I passeil fermement en terre entre ses cuixes, et lie drapelz entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide; puis teigne li ministres la cuixe, et uns autres ministres estende lou piet a ses mains ou a I liien, k’il lie sus le col dou piet; puis estende chescuns ministres igalment, et li passelz soit adés entre les cuixes dou malaide por retenir le malaide quant on l’estent; puis mette li mires igal la dislocation a ses mains, et uns autres ministres teigne la jambe sainne au desoz, et li dislocation revenra hastanment.	 And when it is completely displaced, one should make the patient lie down flat on their back with legs extended; then grasp the foot in your right hand, and then at the heel twice, then extend upwards firmly placing the foot above; do this twice as we have said, pushing and pulling the foot; if it returns, that's good; if not, resume the treatment because it will return; and if it cannot be returned thus, make the patient lie on their back with their legs in between two people pressing firmly into the ground, a cloth around them to prevent movement of the body, then grasp the thigh, and other attendants extend the leg towards you or your line, so that another supports above the neck of the foot; then they should equally distribute the force using both hands, and the grip be maintained between the buttocks of the patient to hold still as the limb is extended; then adjust the splint at its original position with their hands, and other attendants place a healthy leg below, and dislocations will return quickly.
Et quant elle iert a point, si met l’emplastre et estoupes sus, et l’estrain forment, et lie lou piet a la jambe, et warde les ners qui sont sus la cheville derrier, que li liiens ne soit trop estrois; puis le laisse II jors ou III, et se li liiens amolist, si l’estrain; puis le deslie au tier jor ou au quart, et deffent a aler lou malaide par IIII jors; et s’il va devant cel termine, ce n’est mie seurtez qu’il ne desalue encor.	 When it has reached this point, place the dressing and plug into it firmly, tie off the leg above the joint, and protect the tendons behind the ankle so that the ties are not too tight; then leave it for two or three days, and if the bindings loosen, re-straighten; then remove on the fourth day or sooner, and prevent walking by four days; and if it moves before this period ends, it is not securely healed.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si covient que tu l’apaises, si com nos avons dit autre part, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if an abscess comes upon it, one must soothe it as we have said elsewhere, until it is healthy again.
des dois	Of dislocations
Quant li doi sont desaluez, si les covient bellement estendre sens travail, et c’est legiere chose.	When the joints are dislocated, they must be extended with ease of effort, and it is a simple thing to do.
Et se li dislocations est en aucun nout dou dos dou piet, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide sus I leu plain ou sus .ie. table tot droit, et met ton piet sus ce qui apert de ces jointures, puis presse a ton piet forment, tant qu’il reviegne; et quant il est igalz, et il n’i apert nient, si met desoz la plante dou piet une table a II chiés, puis l’estrain forment, et le laisse III jors, puis le deslie; et le fai reposer, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 If the dislocation is in any of your back or leg joints, it's necessary to have the patient sit upright or on a flat table and place their foot below these joints, then press firmly under their foot with two fingers; when it returns evenly, without anything protruding, put a splint beneath the sole of the foot, straighten forcefully, leave for three days, then remove. Let them rest until healed.
de plaie et de dislocation ensamble	Of wound and of dislocation together
Quant plaie vient avec la dislocation, et on la vuet restorer, maintes fois avient que li malaides muert: si ne soies mie presumptuous en la cure, se tu n’es saiges en l’art et tu ne l’as useit longement, et se tu n’es pitous et misericors et tardis, ne mie hardis; et use au comencement de choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et laisse le malaide en la main Deu, se tu n’i vois esperance de santeit; et quant tu i vois esperance, si ramoinne maintenant le membre au leu, ainsois que li apostemes chaus i viegne; et quant li membres est a leu, si aministre choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et cure la plaie, si com il covient, d’oignemens desiccatis; et se avec la dislocation a brisure, et os menus desevrez, si les oste, et fai ce que nos avons dit en maladies simples; et te garde d’entrer en voie de paour, selonc ce que j’ai dit, car ce te vaut mues selonc ton Creator, et por la saveteit de t’arme et de ton cors.	 When a wound comes with dislocation and needs to be restored, many times the patient dies: do not presume in treatment if you are not wise in the art and have not practiced it long, unless you are compassionate, merciful, and slow; also cautious at first with soothing treatments for abscesses, and let the patient rely on God's hand if there is no hope of health; and when there is hope, reset the limb to its place now, as soon as the abscess heats up; and when the limb is in place, administer calming remedures for the abscess, treat the wound as needed with dried ointments; and if there is dislocation with fracture, and small bones are dislodged, follow what we have said in simple ailments; and beware of entering into fear's way, as I have said, for it serves you according to your creator, and for the healthiness of your armor and body.
